This is a really well done Star Wars strategy game that does a good job of capturing the feel of the original trilogy, letting you sort of create your own Star Wars story that still feels like Star Wars. Combat feels a bit tedious, fleets feel very slow as they only move one space a turn without special cards, and the board doesn't exactly adhere to cannon (Geonosis and Felucia weren't populated during the OT era. Why not use Lothal, Kuat, Eriadu, etc?), which is sort of annoying, but those are my only complaints about the game, really. It's really good.

RATING: 9
Loved it. Now need to settle into a few more games to see if it truly holds up. There's quite a bit to explore yet - not to mention playing *both* sides of the conflict. If one is seeking flaws, I think there are three. First, the game is quite long - allow 3+ hours for a first play (and it may not go down much with repeated plays). Second, there are small corner cases with cards that create conflicts to be resolved mainly by common sense. Third, the order in which you draw cards has a significant effect on the potential of the outcome. Still, the game is wonderful and is the definitive dramatic implementation of Star Wars. The *only* significant drawback is the length of play.

EDIT: One take back with this one is there really *isn't* much combat - that the game is deceptive in that way. The miniatures seem to scream old 80's games of smashing ships against one another. But in fact, combat isn't as important as deception (for the Rebellion) and fear (for the Empire). It's more a cat and mouse game than a conquest game. When combat does happen (perhaps 3-4 significant times), it is at times clunky to resolve.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Star Wars: Rebellion is an action selection game masquerading as a war game.  While the fleet actions and combat are an important element of the game, the crux of the game is the use of the game's leaders.  The Rebels are not going to win a war campaign against the Empire.  Instead, they have to use clever planning and strategy to survive the Imperial onslaught and buy time to rally the galaxy to their side.  On the Imperial side, the war game is much more important, but as an occupying force, the Empire cannot clump their ships and troops together to crush the Rebel fleets, but must spread out their forces to ensure find the Rebel base and prevent the Rebels from going to ground if found.

The game is dripping with Star Wars theme.  All the main characters from the original trilogy are there and your odds of seeing them in most games are high.  The events, objectives, projects, and action cards all fit the game's flavor.  The artwork and models are all spot-on, and seeing everything on the board engrosses you in the theme.

The game does have its downsides.  First, it is long, likely taking a good 4-6 hours to play.  That may not be a hurdle to some people, but for me it will mean the game is a special occasion type of game, rather than a regular game night favorite.

Second, there is a fair helping of randomness in the game with the use of dice in mission attempts and combat, but you'll be rolling dice frequently enough that luck should balance out for both sides.  And I think the more experienced, more strategic-minded player will win the majority of the time.

And third, the replayability of the game might not quite be what you might expect from a $100 game.  I've played twice, both times as the Rebels, and so have seen most of the cards that side has to offer come up during games.  The second game definitely did not feel the same as the first, and I think it would not feel samey if you only play once a month or less, but if you were to play it weekly, it might get tiring before too long.  I think the game will stand up to multiple plays, but I wouldn't turn down an expansion with some added missions and objectives.

One last area I wanted to address is the multiplayer rules.  I have played the game both as a 2 player and a 4 player game, and I liked both very much.  I was skeptical about the multiplayer rules, because they seemed tacked on to what would be best as a 1 vs 1 game, but they really turned out to be a lot of fun.  The snaking turn order really adds an extra wrinkle to the game, and both players feel like they have enough responsibilities to feel like an equal team.  Granted I played the game with a cooperative partner, so if you end up with a selfish or bossy partner, your experience may be ruined, but I put that on the player and not the game.

Rebellion is a great "event" game, i.e. one to be played infrequently on special occasions.  I liked it much more than my recent play of Twilight Imperium 3, and I would even prefer it to something like Star Wars: Imperial Assault.  It might be hard for some to justify $100 for a game that will not see the table often, but if it fits your budget and you are a Star Wars fan, this is a must-have.

RATING: 8
Initial rating.  This one will probably go up with more plays.  My buddy and I figure this game takes about 3 plays to understand the cards, strategies, and interactions.

Thematically, this nails Star Wars in a way that others do not.  [thing=939]The Queen's Gambit[/thing] is pretty good, but really just a luck fest based on crappy source material.  [thing=3284]Epic Duels[/thing] sucks.  The miniature game is alright, but has no ships.  But this one has it all -- from the good Star Wars movies.  It has oodles of cool plastic.  It has theme (find the hidden rebel base and destroy it!) it has characters, cards, and chits.  It is not overly complicated to learn but is not overly simple in strategy.

This is for the Star Wars universe what [thing=115746]War of the Ring[/thing] is for the Lord of the Rings' universe.  Is it as epic and awesome as WotR?  Time will tell.

RATING: 10
This game is drenched in theme—from destroying a Death Star with a "one in a million" shot and staging daring rescues with the Millennium Falcon to inexorably subjugating the galaxy and converting Rebel heroes to the Dark Side of the Force. Other than War of the Ring, there's nothing out there that so completely immerses you in the epic feel of the source material.

The strategy feels extraordinarily deep, too. No two games are the same, because there are so many different paths to victory depending on the board state, your opponent, your leaders, where you've chosen to hide the Rebel base (or think it's hidden), etc. And despite some rumblings to the contrary, I find the combat system quite enjoyable. A fantastic game!

(area control, 3x)

RATING: 9
FAVOURITE GAME - an epic space battle between the Empire and the Rebel Alliance. As in the video game it is based on, the Empire has to find the secret rebel base, while the Rebels have to gain loyalty in order to outlast the Empire's schemes. In the game you'll take your leaders and send them on mission to gain support, to build, even to fire the mighty Death Star, and also to move your fleets between systems and combat the enemy. The game is all about hard decisions, and card management. The combat is straightforward: the winner takes it all. Up until the last moment, everything is tensed. But, it can take up to three hours and that can be a hindering fact.

RATING: 8
1st play - Star Wars in a box - completely perfect description.  The Imperial forces are all over the Galaxy, and their size works against them.  It's hard to marshal troops in any one area, and the Rebels could be anywhere.  Toe to toe the Empire destroys the Rebels but completely thematically the Rebels are hard to force to a battle.  They're just strong enough to hold off small skirmish fights, and the missions take from all three movies - Sith corrupting Rebel leaders, Luke trains with Yoda, and the Death Star slowly builds.  Very satisfying thematic romp through the whole Star Wars story.

2nd play - This time I played as the Rebels and the experience is awesome.  The feeling of being completely outgunned and outmanned the entire time, forced to resort to guerilla tactics.  It's great fun to use the Empire's size and lack of agility against itself.   Trying to draw attention away from the hidden rebel base, a failed assault on the Death Star and a daring rescue on a captured Princess Leia rounded out the thematic experience.  The only downside to this game is the length, but the time flies by because the game doesn't drag.

Warning: The rules for this game are a disappointment. You will need to read both the "Larn to Play" and "Rules Referrence" guides to play it correctly.  While not too complex, there are several small rules with a HUGE impact on the game if you play them incorrectly or miss using them. That said...

The theme comes across so well in this game that even the most critical Star Wars Universe fans will apprciate this game and mild fans of that universe will appreciate it. First 2 player game took a solid 7 hours and didn't have a lot of looking up rules or AP.  Onthe bright side, it was so fun we played another right after and it only took 4:40.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I see the fanboys have been skewing the BGG ratings...again. Oh, and the Fantasy Flight drones too!

Star Wars: Rebellion is a game that caused an emotional rollercoaster—and maybe not entirely the good kind. First, I have to say that our initial game could not be completed. Due to some reasons that I'll be listing in the CONS section of this review, but mostly it was how slow to start the game is and how long it would be. It was basically eating up the table for a whole day, so we walked away. For a week. Never finished that game. After finally getting to play this game for a long time, I'm ready to chip in with what I think. Let's start with the good.

PROS:
• Nice, big board. Linen quality cards. Cool plastics ("meh" quality). Cool art (no screenshots!)
• Both sides play legitimately differently. IMO, this is a pro not a con. That's why you would even buy this game.
• Tight, but not choked, actions. I really hate games where you're choked for actions each turn. The game starts a bit choked, gets tight, then loosens up by a lot near the end.
• Sense of legitimate pacing if the Rebel player can hack it.
• Genuine moments of euphoria from successfully finding/hiding/relocating the base, misdirecting, mind games, or just pulling off a mission that seems like a bit of a long shot.

CONS:
• The randomness in this game is off the charts. I'm much more critical of this due to it being so tactical. What frustrates the shit out of me about this game is how it feels like Terra Mystica (a game I HATE) combined with globs of randomness (something I HATE and doesn't go with the game type at all). I can't stress this enough: Both players have random mission decks they draw randomly from, the objective cards are randomly drawn, there are two combat tactics card decks you can randomly draw from, and every single combat is random dice with "Fantasy Flight" syndrome where they have extremely low chances of success like some old 80's game before we knew how to make combat fun. This will be the longest point in the review and single-handedly kills the replay value of this game for me in a big way. Randomness doesn't have to kill a game, but FFG sure knows how to make it happen every time without fail.

• NO THEME. How fucking ironic that a game about theme has no theme. It's clearly and blatantly pasted-on when you teleport Emperor Palpatine into a Rebel loyal system to change it to Imperial control with: no ships; no support; an entire Rebel ARMADA there; no assassination of this lone dude; no recourse; no real ability to stop it. Everything in the entire game is like this. It's like someone took a basic abstract strategy game with nonsensical logic, pasted a Star Wars theme on it, then loaded it up with dice and cards so we wouldn't notice how bizarre it was.

• The "oppose" system was clearly designed by a monkey typing randomly on a typewriter. You have to spend your actions to DICE ROLL to try to stop one opponent's action. Sure, it's nice for Rebels who want to stall the game out but god damn it's just shitty, boring, and way too random. If you don't want a particular mission to go off and fail to oppose, you lose your action AND it goes off. This is the most ill-conceived shit I've seen in a game to date.

• The Empire can win instantly with a combination of minor movement and some cards on Turn 1 by getting really lucky. Even if the Rebel player is omnisciently good at picking the rebel base. This never happened to us but it could have easily and almost did twice.

• The Rebels win by making the game as boring as possible: drawing the game out to be even longer. And they probably WILL win if you have competent players, but unfortunately:

• No one can do any setup or make ANY moves until they read every single card in all the tactics decks, mission decks, plan deck, action decks, know every face of every die, what every planet can produce, and so on. EVERYTHING. Want proof? The strongest opening move for the Rebels is Turn 1 Mon-Mothma's ability (which is RANDOMLY given to you) on Utapau, then start the entire Rebel fleet there. This guarantees you 2 Calamari Cruisers, which are equal to Star Destroyers in power. If you can also take Mustafar/Mon-Calamari turn 2, you get more of them which completely changes the game to your favor. But you won't know that without her ability and knowing every single planet. You also have to GET OFF that planet because the Empire has the most broken card in the entire game, which you need to know about:

• SHOW OF POWER. FUCK WHOMEVER DESIGNED THIS CARD.

• Once you get past the very "Fantasy-flightness" about the cards and really grok them, they're not so bad. The biggest problem is how much studying you have to do until everything falls into place and the missions (and their efficacy) become understandable. I suppose that's a learning curve issue, but ingame it feels like a fun issue instead. This game is just not first-timer friendly in any capacity. It's not hard at all, it just requires bookwork like you wouldn't believe.

• If either player is getting more than one "3-Build-Queue" set of ships placed per game, the Rebel player fucked up or got chance-sacked. It would be rare for all but maybe the last turn of the game to see another 3-build set of units come out. That really means the game is hyper-choked on units, even though they kind of feel like a waterfall for the Empire.

• INCREDIBLY cutthroat. Plus on top of that, the cutthroat can just turn out downright dirty if you also get favored by chance at the same time. Go into this game knowing that there will be lamentations and gnashing of teeth. Troops will spawn on top of your weakest places and wipe them out, despite it being a good position. You will randomly lose loyalty to a system RIGHT before you were going to use it to complete a mission. Objectives will blindly be pulled from under the Rebels' nose by an unaware Imperial. This makes the game a really tough sell: Wargames do cutthroat better and tactical mindgames feel like shit with cutthroat. Not sure what SW:R was trying to do here.

Overall, despite the numerous CONs to the game, SW:R has some legitimately "worth-it" moments peppered into the shitpile of randomness, rage, and tedium. I don't think being a fan of SW should ever dictate whether you buy this game. You have to be a fan of hide-and-seek, not mind fantasy flight games, and have a friend who's willing to dive into the deep end immediately.

P.S. Fuck you "Shut Up and Sit Down" team for telling us not to look at the decks because HURR DURR SURPRISES! I wish I could hate you to death.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
I really enjoy this game, I think the mechanisms are intuitive, the game flows well, it's very strategic, every action makes sense, and I feel like every bit of the game meshes together very well. However, the game does drag a bit and if you play this game with someone who in the slightest might not enjoy longer games or is not a very experienced gamer, their confusion and ultimate dislike of the game really makes it unplayable. I have no one to play this game with and it's unlikely I'll find someone anytime soon, so that's why my rating is averaged out to where it is.

RATING: 10
Deeply thematic with fairly complex but well designed rules.  Playing as the Rebels, you really do get a sense of their plight, and how hard it is to avoid detection and capture by the Imperials.  As the Imperials, you have a mighty fleet at your disposal (you start with a fully armed and operational battle station, the Death Star!), along with a fair number of systems under your control.  On some turns the Imperials will be able to produce more units than the Rebels start with!  Both factions offer an entirely asymmetrical experience, with entirely different goals.  Can the Imperials find and destroy the hidden Rebel base before the Rebels can sway the rest of the galaxy against the Imperials.  There's only one way to find out!

RATING: 5
7/7/16: The Theme is strong in this one.  First impressions, needlessly complicated.  Playing teams can get very frustrating.  Like all FFG games, you're buying this for the theme, not the gameplay.  If you don't love Star Wars, I'd stay away from this.  If you're used to wargames, the clunky and swingy combat will be frustrating.

Only FFG  would have come up with dice symbols meaning one thing on one type of roll, and something else on another roll.

What you do get is a very thematic game, with a great story and a ton of great plastic.  You do need to learn what possibilities are made available via the cards, the first time through you're just trying to learn the game.  The cards do cause some wild swings, but that's the nature of the game.

I think that the length is going to kill it for me, but will need more plays to really know.  I don't mind 4 hours of Fury of Dracula, because you're working with a team, but here where it's just one on one, it's a little long for what it offers.  It may also be that I'm slowly burning out on the FFG game style where so much of the game is on cards.  The tactics cards in this game really remind me of the Battlestar Galactica game where your card draws really determine everything.

I don't think that 4 player works all that well unless you have 2 people that work really well together.  The rolls aren't that well defined, and you have to go through everything together which slows things down further..


Learning 2 player game: 4 hours, 4 player game 5.5 hours

RATING: 9
Where to start that hasn't already been said?

This game is War of the Ring for the Star Wars universe. It captures the FEEL of the original trilogy very well. There's some great bluffing, great push-your-luck mechanics and a wonderful cat-and-mouse game between the Empire and Alliance.

It's one of those games that if you were to play 100 games of it with the same person, individual strategies would arise between the two of you - expected bases, methods of lockdown from the imperials, and ways to counter those strategies.

However, due to the length of the game, I don't think anyone will ever saturate the iterations needed to know the game that well.

A big complaint a lot of people have is the combat. However, I don't see it as too bad - it doesn't take long, and is easy enough to learn. It can be a bit of a dice-fest, but that isn't too much of a problem because it isn't central to the game.

Can't wait to play this one more.

RATING: 8
Több okból is úgy ültem neki, hogy a WOTR játékkal való összevetést szem előtt tartottam. Már eleve úgy ajánlották, hogy ez is egy jóféle aszimmetrikus játék, ráadásul itt is hasonlóan a "jó oldal" játékában a rejtőzködésen van a fő hangsúly, míg a "rossz oldal" a nagy harci erejére épít.

Röviden: nem a WOTR-hoz kellett volna viszonyítani, mert önmagában nézve tök jó játék a Rebellion, de ha a kettő közül kéne választanom, egyértelműen a WOTR mellé ülnék le szívesebben. Mind monumentalitásában, mind az eredeti ötletek terén, mind a szabály letisztultságában, mind hangulatban, de még változatosság ígéretében is (néhány partit játszottam csak mindkettővel) a Gyűrűk háborúja a Lázadás fölé nő. Amott a Gyűrűhordozás rejtőzködő mechanizmusa egészen különleges, cserébe itt is van egy egész jó Kutászkodás, de nekem azért ez picit laposabb.

De hogy ne csak összehasonlítsak: A Rebellion egy jól összerakott, élvezetes játék, aminek átjön a hangulata. A küldetésekhez kiküldött vezetők egy tök jó taktikai részt visznek a játékba, jól kell elosztani a vezetőket, számítani kell meglepetésekre a másik oldalról. Tetszik, hogy a kockadobós részek nincsenek túlbonyolítva: mind a csatáknál, mind a küldetéseknél csak 3-4 kimenet lehetséges, nincsen kismillió módosító, igaz a sebzéseket meg azok kivédését a kártyákkal kicsit egzaktabbul is leszabályozhatták volna. Az egységek gyártása jól ki van találva, a Halálcsillag meg teljes egészében tematikusan van megoldva, tetszik. Amikor fenyegetve volt a bázisom, mindent megtettem, hogy a feladatok közül valahogy megszerezzem a "Halálcsillag tervek" lapot, különben game over. Izgalmas kör volt, mivel azt túléltem, még 3 órán át tartott a parti. Ez érdekes egyébként, hogy nagy pech, vagy rossz bázis választás esetén lehet nagyon rövid is a parti, de akár 4-5 órás is.

A szabály külön megemlíti azt hiszem a jótanácsoknál, hogy a Lázadó játékos ne törődjön azzal, hogy esetleg szinte teljesen lesöpörték már a térképről, úgy van felépítve a játék, hogy ettől még nyerhető a Lázadókkal, csak néhány hírnévpontot kell összekaparni és rejtőzködni még néhány kört. Ez a része nagyon tetszik. A minik is jók.

A gyűrűk, amiket a szereplőkre tehetünk, nagyon jópofák, de a technikai kivitelezés zavar, nem szeretem, ha sérülnek a játékelemek. A magyar kiadásról még néhány szó: néhányan túllihegték szerintem a fordítással kapcsolatos bénázásokat. Persze én is örültem volna, ha nem kell még házilag javításokat nyomtatgatni, de így is bőven a pozitív oldalon van a kiadás. Rendelkezem a játékhoz szükséges angollal, mégsem vettem volna meg szerintem, ha nem adják ki magyarul, mert így a családban is ki tudom próbálni esetleg.

Összefoglalva: SW fanoknak kötelező, de mindenki próbálja ki szerintem, aki szereti a 2 személyes komolyabb játékokat. 4 személlyel nem tudom, milyen lehet.

RATING: 7.5
This is the most epic game ever made with the Star Wars license: a two-player struggle between the Galactic Empire and the Rebellion, encompassing the whole civil war.

It is essentially a card driven game, with leaders assigned to mission cards as the main mechanic, so it is necessary to memorize (or at least have a more than vague idea about) the cards in each deck.
The political control and resource/unit production are both simple and elegant, while the combat system is a bit clunky and time-consuming (but not too-much convoluted).

The length of the game will keep it from hitting the table too much, but when it does, it's epicness will unravel in all its magnificence... Well done, FFG!

RATING: 8
Initial Impression: FFG has done it again. A highly thematic game with wonderfully produced components treats this Star Wars IP properly. This is without a doubt my favorite of the Star Wars games that FFG has produced. It's akin to a wargame but can be taught quickly and played within a reasonable amount of time for a game of this epic scale. I particularly enjoy the cat-n-mouse game of locating the rebel base. The game is a wonderful blend of strategic decisions for both the Empire and Rebellion, as well as tactical choices with a healthy dose of bluffing. Tying all actions/missions to leaders is a brilliant way to limit operations in the game, while tying the mechanisms closely to the theme. There's almost a CDG feel to this game. I'm very tempted to add this game to my collection, and probably will at some point in the future.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
This is the Star Wars Saga in a Box. While Imperial Assault or X-Wing are concerned with small skirmishes, in Rebellion you either represent the whole galactic empire or the band of rebels trying to bring back a senate republic. The empire tries to find the location of the rebel base and wipe it out. The rebels try to hide from the empire long enough in order to win more support in the senate. 

Players plan simultaneously which characters they want to send on tasks to the different planets. These tasks include things like winning support of the system (area control), taking prisoners from the other side, building a super star destroyer or moving the rebel base to a new system. Some characters are left without tasks. They are used to move ships and land units across the board. Despite both sides having a military win conditon, only the empire has a chance of winning this way. The rebels try to hide long enough and fulfill some missions/assignments that shorten the time that has to pass in order for them to win.
All the tasks and missions feel so thematic. Luke Skywalker can go to Dagoba to look for Yoda. If he finds him then Luke becomes a Jedi and is replaced by a stronger character pawn. The empire can develop the main weapon on the death star and blow up planets - hopefully containing the rebel base. 
There is a ton of player interaction with some dice rolling for combat and sometimes to see if a task/mission is accomplished or if the enemy side did interfere successfully. The rebel player constantly fears that the empire finds the location of his rebel base - tense.

The box says 2-4 players but I would only play it as a 2-player game. It takes some time (also to set it up) but it gets you in the zone for the whole time. I suggest you turn on any of the Star Wars Soundtracks while playing.

People who like the theme, area control, simultaneous action selection, dice based combat and miniatures will have a blast - pun intended.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Yes it's "Star Wars in box." And it's enjoyable if you like games that heavily lean on theme. I find it a little long for what it is though, and don't think has the legs a fairly epic game like this should have. It's cool when it twists on the events of the movies, but that novelty quickly wears off. A good time, but I don't get a charge out of it like I do some other favorites of this length.

RATING: 10
Awesome game. Greatly exceeds the 90s computer game of the same name. I really love the asymmetric nature of the game. The Rebels simply cannot beat the Empire through military might alone, as it should be. Minis are fantastic. The gameplay is well-balanced.

There are only two real downsides to this game. The first is that the rulebook is not very well-written. The first few games will likely involve a lot of confusion and flipping through pages. The second is that it really is only designed for 2 players, regardless of what it says on the box. The rules for additional players feel like they were hastily tacked-on and don't seem to work very well.

RATING: 9
This is Episode 4-6 in a box. Hugely thematic. Hugely asymmetric. It really gives the feel of the military might of the Empire going up against a shadow war and tactical strikes coming from the Rebellion. Great storylines as you move your leaders across the board. For example: Rebels recruit Wedge, Wedge gets captured, Palpatine turns Wedge, Wedge leads final attack on Rebel base. Hidden base mechanic and probe deck is very engaging to play out. Very deep strategy regarding where you use your leaders. Only con is that games can feel too similar if you draw the same mission cards, but that's minor. I don't have an issue with the combat other than wanting more variety of tactic cards. Yes it can take multiple rounds. Yes  it can be complicated, but simulating an entire land/space invasion in a single combat should be complex. Combat happens infrequently enough that it should be epic.

RATING: 10
Absolutely majestic. I was unprepared for how epic, tense and engrossing this game was going to be. It really is the trilogy in a box. I played the Empire and just ached to crush the Rebels. I felt my power sprawling about the galaxy. The game went long - about five hours - but it went by in the blink of an eye. It also very much evokes the feel of War of the Ring in the Star Wars universe but with more approachable Star Wars mechanics and a more intuitive "Hunt" sequence. Do the space battles interrupt the main game - do they involve fewer decisions? The answer is a "yes, but." So much rests on breath-in-throat player decisions that it's almost a relief to have a battle of good old dice chucking interspersing the main board action. It offers a catharsis for both players to see things happen and units blown up. If it were any more demanding, it might become more of distracting mini-game (and I might get exhausted before game end). Perfect realization of the Star Wars narrative; perfect game.

RATING: 8.5

The weakest point is the limited options to each player, who are mostly on rail due to their card draw or the current board state. RATING: 3
Might be irreversibly ruined for me, knowing it was loosely based on the 90s computer game of the same name. That game was fantastic, and this system simply doesn't have any of that decision space. This simply isn't Star Wars; it's something else entirely, with $70 of Star Wars bling slapped onto it.

- The game track makes zero thematic sense.

- There is zero interrelation between space and ground units other than the odd tactic card. No orbital bombardment? Come on.

- No hyperspace to speak of, really ... Except a very limited element associated with the Rebel base. All adjacent planets are the same distance away from one another, and there are no solar systems to speak of.

- No assymetric production like one would expect from Rebels v. Empire.

- The hard dice limit of five per color makes no sense thematically.

- The minimized difference in ship capabilities is annoying at best, and horribly arbitrary at worst. The SSD is only 1.5 times better than the ISD, even though it's ten times longer?

- The arbitrary limitations set throughout the rulebook are frustrating, and serve to only limit the flexibility of the media provided. There's no thematic reason to have only one Rebel captured at a time, and there's also no thematic reason why Rebel can take prisoners of their own.

All of which serves to just suggest this was a fine game during its inception, but someone down the line realized they could make a killing by making it a Star Wars game, so they slapped the theme on.

RATING: 8
It took a few games to grow on me, but now that I understand the flow of the game better, I really, really like it. I actually kind of disliked it after my first play, and even considered selling it at that point. I think this was simply because the game went on longer than anticipated, and it was hard to nail down what strategies I should be employing. But I've also learned much each game, and that has improved my skill and enjoyment of every subsequent game. I've lost every game up to this point (2x as Rebellion, 1x as Empire) and to the same person (mark my words Alex, I will win eventually!), but they still ended up being enjoyable and worthwhile experiences.

I recommend to anyone who loves Star Wars, enjoys multi-hour games, wants a unique experience, likes asymmetry, and is open to playing a few games before being able to fully comprehend what they're supposed to be doing.

Some notes after another play several months later:
*This can be a long game! That's probably the main factor holding my rating at an 8. It just takes too long to want to play all the time (granted, I am a slow player, so perhaps this is mostly a personal issue).
*This game gets better and smoother the more the players are familiar with the cards, leaders, etc. Coming back to it after having not played for many months makes me kinda feel like an inexperienced player again as there are many important intricacies present that can be easily overlooked if you're not already "in the groove".

War of the Ring and Star Wars made a baby? Hell yeah!
After reading the rules it looked more like a lighter TI3 or Runewars combined with the asymmetry...blabla.

IT'S STAR WARS!!! EPIC SCALE!!!

It looks heavier than it is. The rules are pretty simple and the game-system is pretty easy to manage while providing enough range for big strategy, meaningful plans and outbluffing each other.

It plays super fast, no downtime, and the playtime is shorter than expected. 2,5 hours are enough.

Great game.

RATING: 6
The video game Star Wars Rebellion was quite fun in spite of an awful interface. It was a computer adaptation of Freedom in the Galaxy released by SPI and then Avalon Hill back in the late '70s. Turning Star Wars Rebellion into a board game doesn't really work as well as the video game because they had to shrink the scale of the universe and conflict to get a reasonable play time. I've played the rebels twice. You don't get enough of anything to make it very much fun. All you do is hide and wait and try to survive to the end. You don't get all the rebel leaders just some, you can't build up much, the cards you can play are pretty generic and bland and it's not uncommon to just be unable to do anything, and combat is a pain in the ass. It makes me wish I would have picked up Freedom in the Galaxy for $5 from KayBee Toys back in 1987 along with the Starship Troopers I bought for $4. While I don't know if that game is playable nowadays at least the scale was right. Why does the empire need to build a super star destroyer? If the rebels could actually put together a fleet with four Mon Calamari cruisers I could see it making sense. I'll play one more time as the Imperial side but I think I'll be done with the game after that and I'm glad I didn't buy it.

RATING: 9
Almost done with the introductory game, playing with my 9 year old son.

Beautifully assymetrical and dripping with Star Wars thematics. My son captured Han Solo, successfully interrogated him, and was certain that he had obliterated the Rebel Base when his Death Star blew up Mon Calamari. But to his surprise, the Rebel Base wasn't there!

After leaving his Death Star unguarded, I launched a surprise attack with a small force of fighters, but Darth Vader managed to turn the tide in his favor and keep the Death Star safe.

Then I launched another surprise attack, but this time a large force of Y-Wings (with X-Wing escorts) managed to take down a lightly defended Star Destroyer in orbit around Coruscant, sending more shockwaves throughout the galaxy and turning many to sympathize with the Rebellion. 

He later retaliated by capturing Obi-Wan Kenobi and encasing him in carbonite, sending shockwaves through the galaxy that countered my efforts to sway systems to the Rebellion.

Now I am seeing the end game coming, and he is far away from my base, and I can't wait to spring Rapid Mobilization on him at the last moment.

Seriously, very fun game.

RATING: 10
nur Geil das Spiel
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
My biggest concern with Rebellion was that the playing time was going to be much to high for it to have legs. Now that I'm up to 4 plays, this has gone from concern to reality. Like all games from this designer, there is just too much crap in the system. Last game I was the Rebels and sitting on 9 leaders and a handful of missions, and basically nothing interesting to do - the missions were inapplicable not doing useful things and I didn't have forces that needed to move. My Imperial opponent was in the same boat. We all knew where the rebel base was, he had about two turns to get enough force there to kill it, and all the rest was screwing around; but there still was a lot of screwing around. The game just has too much flab and bloat and it comes through with a 4 hour playing time, of which about 2 is actually interesting. As always, the principal culprit here is the mission deck: too few are generally interesting, too many don't make enough difference to generate interest, and you don't cycle enough of them to feel like you have real choices - you just go on all the missions you get, and hope it works out. If you're the Imperials and get the carbon-freezing mission that's great, if you don't ever draw it that means the game is one fewer turn and you probably lose.

In general, the game just had very little sense of dynamism. Military operations take place at an excruciatingly slow pace. Forces take forever to concentrate. While Han and Luke got from Tatooine to Alderaan in a matter of hours, not days, in the game it's the work of the entire length of the game for military forces to make that same trip. Missions rarely pack enough punch to be interesting. There just is no "bomb" in the game, the dynamic event that really changed things up and makes for excitement or anticipation or fear. There is just the long slow grind to the end.

Lastly, and probably most problematically, Rebellion seems like basically a 1-player game. The Imperials will win or lose. It's not clear that the Rebels do very much that really makes any difference. The Imperials have lots of variables to juggle: they need to find the rebel base, they need to manage their economy to generate enough forces, they need to block the Rebels activities, and they need to pursue the super-weapons projects. The Rebels just need to do a few obvious things - try to get some loyalty down, win a few local victories - and basically they succeed where the Imperials allow them to, or where they roll well. They just don't have a ton of agency. The Imperials will win if they successfully balance all their competing interests (pretty hard), and lose otherwise. What the rebels do does not seem to be all that relevant.

I could suspend my disbelief for a while, and hope that Rebellion wouldn't fall prey to all the crippling design problems that every game Konieczka has had. But no. The pace is leaden, too much of the model makes no sense, it's weirdly over-complicated in some ways (although in general Rebellion is petty playable, it's just got a bunch of weird edge cases and the combat system is a mess), the theme isn't that much more than fan service, and it has very little intensity or engagement. Compared to any other decent 4 hour wargame (any No Retreat game, EastFront, Hannibal, Caucuses Campaign), Rebellion just feels really overwrought, slack, and uncompelling.

Anyway, with Fantasy Flight you know what you're getting these days. If you like Battlestar Galactica or Descent, you might like Rebellion. If not, give it a miss. Yeah, it's Star Wars, but all the weird ways in which it's not Star Wars will start to annoy you pretty quickly. Stick to X-Wing.

---
My take on some things Rebellion does well, and some it doesn't: https://li.st/l/63c4db68-9cec-43e8-88ae-b9e12eaeeb70

Although it's not that similar, Rebellion's closest analog is War of the Ring. I actually think it's better than WotR, but I didn't like WotR that much. 
---
Just one play, but you'll be as shocked as I am to hear me say that this seems to show some real promise! The game plays pretty cleanly and gives you a bunch of interesting trade-offs, and manages to maintain some interesting game tension. It captures some fun stuff from the classic trilogy, and while it's not in the same tightly thematic league as Knizia's Lord of the Rings or Middle-Earth: The Wizards, it's pretty solid.

The risk is that FFG usually doesn't do the heavy lifting to get the nuts-and-bolts card balance and narrative tension of its games right. So there is still a lot of risk (in my mind anyway) associated with the mission cards, and whether as the Imperials you need to pursue a balanced approach, or if it's really just a "probe droids all the way then blow up the Rebel Base" kind of a thing. I kinda think it might be. But at the very least you'll probably need to do some kind of holding action to keep the Rebel objectives at bay, so there is adequate reason to hope. On the Rebel side, there is some question as to whether it's worth the opportunity cost and hassle to upgrade Luke to a Jedi, or pursue some other plot lines they actually did in the movies, but time will tell on that.

The narrative cohesion is actually pretty good, certainly better than previous games by this designer and FFG in general. You get a little bit of a rational flow to the missions and such which gives it a bit of a narrative pulse. Still - weird choices. Why, for example, is it not a mission to steal the Death Star plans? You get the plans from an Objective. Certainly far from game-breaking, just another one of those odd choices that FFG routinely makes in their games.

It is a bit long, I think longer than it really wants to be. Plan on probably 4+ hours your first time out, with a potential to run 5+. Not great; there is not so much depth here that it justifies a playing time that much over 3hr. But not too bad either. Battlestar Galactica was punishingly over-long, and this is not in that league. It's definitely not super-tight game, but it's not too bad.

Anyway, that's some random thoughts. I enjoyed my first game, and I look forward to playing it again. There are still some obvious long-term risks, but also some significant potential. It's obviously designed to be significantly expanded; if, for example, Rogue One works out it would be fun to get some of the characters and events from the new movie into the game (especially since it looks like there are a few women in the cast in leading roles, which the game sadly lacks; not including Howlrunner on the Imperial side, especially given how high-profile she is in FFG's X-Wing, was a huge oversight).

----

Intriguing to see a few nods to the classic SPI/AH Freedom in the Galaxy, which was Star Wars with the serial numbers filed off. Could be a coincidence.

This is actually a totally great premise for a game, and there are a number of really interesting ways you could go with it. Clearly the core structure of Freedom in the Galaxy is basically correct for one political/military angle, but since that game was unplayable even in the 80s, you'd want to pick and choose what you want to do, and have an interesting angle. Unfortunately, the in-house designers at FFG seem to be fuck-ups, so what we'll likely get is some half-assed plastic monster which doesn't really work (see: Merchant of Venus, Rex, Mansions of Madness, too many others to count). I'll play it once just to see how they screw it up, but hold out no optimism.

RATING: 8.9
Phenomenal game of cat and mouse.  This is Scotland Yard/Letters From Whitechapel/Fury of Dracula melded with a dudes on a map game.  The whole thing is tied together with a really unique worker placement-ish mission system where you assign limited commander assets each turn to narrative missions or use them to move about the board and fight.

Playtime is extremely long (3 hours) but it flows very well and feels only like an hour has passed.  Very engaging and exciting.  Full of drama.

The only weak point I found was the combat, which isn't bad.  It merely is a bit bland and not up to the excellence of the rest of the design.

RATING: 5
Based on 1 play with 2 players:

This is one of those games that is INCREDIBLY difficult to rate after just one play, so it feels wrong to start of with "I'm not sure I understand the hype here" but that's all I can think of so there ya go.

Essentially it felt like this game isn't sure what it wants to be. It tries to marry a tense bluffing game with a galactic conquest game to mixed success. It seems like bluffing ought to be the heart of the game, but most of the systems tie more meaningfully into the conquest game which is frankly lacking.

The takeaway here is that the action resolution and combat systems are just plain dull. Roll some dice, who got lucky? Wheeeeeeee. And that's like, 70% of the game.

Again, having only played once we spent most of the game trying to wrap our heads around the rules (the subjugation vs loyalty system was pretty fuzzy for us for most of the game) so there may very well be more interesting ways to bluff and deduce than I'm giving this game credit for - but this first play absolutely did not have the same kind of tension you would find in, say, a hidden movement game. Ultimately it just comes down to feeling like there are more tense and exciting cat-and-mouse games and way better conquest games (Konieczka's own Forbidden Stars for example), so it's hard to want to spend 2-3 hours on this.

RATING: 9
The most perfectly balanced game I have played!
There are so many ways to play and so many things to do you can try something new each time.
Both sides play differently, too, with obvious strengths to use and weaknesses for your opponent to exploit.

The dice add a random factor which some people have incorrectly attributed to a reliance on luck. But careful use of your cards and characters can still put things firmly in your favour. Your resources are essential - many of your cards are one-use only so you need to pick the right moment. If you're relying on just a dice roll, you're playing it wrong!

The promotional material promised a game that was cinematic in scope and it doesn't disappoint, whether you're turning Mon Mothma to the Dark Side on Ord Mandell or having Luke Skywalker lead a Rogue Squadron strike on a Star Destroyer being constructed above Sullust, each game tells a story.

The use of heroes to drive the game works really well and fits the Star Wars setting perfectly. The placement of heroes, their unique abilities and strengths in combat, form the chief mechanic, but they can't be everywhere at once, making allocating characters an important task.

In a nutshell, it manages to achieve everything it claims to be, which is pretty special.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is the best game I have played in many years. 

In 3-4 hours, you play one encounter. The conflict is asymmetric; the Empire has more forces, but a limited time to find and destroy the Rebel base. The Rebel player need only delay the Empire until time runs out, but can make that clock go faster by meeting objectives. Even after 10 games, I'm still learning things and seeing new strategies. 

The rules are pretty well written, so after your first game most of your time will be spent playing and thinking. There are a lot of decisions to make, and the better player wins a vast majority of the time.

The tactical part (how many forces to send into an attack, or how to assign damage during a battle) is very minor. A bigger part for the Empire is planning: where do I position fleets, and how do I defend my territories from raids. Both sides must make Go-like decisions. Where do I want to fight or escalate, and where should I ignore? The Rebel player has to balance maximizing the safety of the hidden rebel base, meeting objectives to accelerate the clock, and confusing/deflecting the Empire's search for the base. 

The game also plays well with 3-4 players (using up to 2 players per side). The subtle changes in the game rules for >2 players significantly changes the strategies.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Pretty much everything I wanted in a strategic Star Wars game.
Where it's too simple, I can use the events as models for miniatures or roleplaying game scenarios. 
Character cards are replaceable with personalized units, but the general mechnics are beautifully accessible.
My only regret is that this game, like its classic DOS predecessor, namesake, and obvious inspiration, is really only two-player.
In this regard, the Risk Star Wars "Saga" edition is slightly superior, and a mash-up of the two results in what is, for me, the perfect Star Wars campaign game.

RATING: 10
This is my first game review as I'm still semi new to board gaming. This game is AMAZING! I bought it on Friday after watching hours of videos and reviews online about it. I'm a huge Star Wars fan and the "Star Wars in a box" tag line got me. So I had a game night with 3 friends last night...we opened up the game and started popping cardboard! 

Myself and another friend had been watching videos online so we had a BASIC understanding of the mechanics. We knew we were in for a long game but we wound up playing for...8 hours! 1 game...8 hours. Now I know that sounds crazy but that includes setting everything up, smoke breaks, food break and of course playing the game. We took our time to make sure we were playing the game correctly. It did not seem like we were playing for that long at all! It was pretty much non stop fun from beginning to end!

My partner and I were the Empire while my 2 other buddy's were the Rebels. Playing as the Empire definitely makes you feel powerful. The whole game I felt as if we were unstoppable. We got overconfident and let the Rebellion sneak in and DESTROY OUR DEATH STAR!  Now normally when something like that happens it illicits anger...nope it was AWESOME! Han Solo led an armada of Mon Kalamari ships and Y-Wings into our system....we thought "no way, what are they thinking?" And then boom! Darth Star plans card is played....we tried to recover (we were in the process of moving towards Tattooine where the Rebel base was located) but simply ran out of time. I have never had so much fun losing a game. 

From trying to freeze Luke in Carbonite to Interrogating Leia to find out where the Rebel Base was this game is very thematic! If you like Star Wars do yourself a favor and RUN to the store to pick it up. May the Force be with you.

RATING: 8
Pros:
- Balanced but highly asymmetrical.
- Action management through leader placement and mission planning stage is satisfying.
- Military unit positioning in galaxy map is important and key to each sides' strategy.
- Tense cat and mouse gameplay.
- Fantastic components.

Cons:
- Combat could be more interesting but the leader card bonus to give an edge to space and/or ground forces is not a bad system. Expansion possibly improves and expands on the combat.
- Rather long game, 3 plus hours for sure.
- Plays best at 2, wouldn't recommend sharing turn duties with the 3-4 player rules.
- Set up takes a while but also is part of the gameplay.

RATING: 9.5
I love this game!  The gameplay is quite simple, yet the amount of actions you are able to do each turn because of how many leaders you have available is what causes it to become quite lengthy.  Yet, that is where the heart of the game lies, in the strategy and planning of which leaders you will send on missions, and to where, because trying to draw out your opponents leaders to oppose your missions may be part of the strategy even more so than wanting to succeed on the mission. . . The combat isn't as complicated as it originally seems, and there is a bit of strategy involved when planning which units to send. I love the tension involved, and the theme is perfect.  It is a long game, so that will make it hard to get out, but it's worth it.

RATING: 9
This is straight up War of the Ring with Star Wars. I don't know why anyone hasn't mentioned this yet in any review. 

You have one overwhelming evil side with tons of resources going trying to overwhelm the good side that basically only win by avoiding the evil side. There is even a mechanic where the Empire searches for the hidden Rebel base which screams "Hunt for the Ring" from War of the Ring.

That all being said, all board games borrow from other board games and I think this one does it well. This is a hell of an excellent game and if you love games like War of the Ring or Battle of the Five Armies, you will love this game. 

Also, components are excellent and Fantasy Flight actually made a decent box for this one that can fit all the components in–a far superior design to the Descent Second Edition box.

This game is worth your time and money.

RATING: 9
Does for Star Wars what War of the Ring does for Tolkien: playing it transports you to the world of the original trilogy. This game is actually a bit simpler than WotR, but takes longer to play. I'm not sure that the depth matches the play time (I feel kind of the same way about WotR in terms of effort, rather than time), but there is so much flavor that I never get bored. Four hours of SW:Rebellion is a really fun four hours.

The components are fantastic, even by FFG standards. Everything is beautiful *and* functional.

I haven't tried this with more than two players, but I assume that the team rules would extend the play time, which is not what this game needs.

On that note, if you don't love Star Wars, don't bother with this unless a light 2-player 4X game that takes all afternoon really appeals to you. (Yes, this is absolutely a 4X game, despite its asymmetry.)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a fun and challenging game. It seems to combine the political control elements of Washington's War with the hero and unit-type dynamics of A Game of Thrones:  The Board Game. The gist of the game is that the Rebel player places a secret base at the beginning, and the Imperial player has to find it. While there are a number of systems to chose from, it seems to me the Rebel player would want to typically place it as far away from Imperial forces as possible—thereby maximizing the amount of time it takes for the Imperial player to get there and poke around. This may limit replayability, but I will have to play more before I decide anything on that point. It is also nice that the game facilitates play from 2-4 players. Be prepared, though: it does not play fast! But it should be enjoyable to any fans of the series, as well as strategy gamers generally.

Interesting asymmetric wargame sees players take on the Empire and the Rebellion in the Star Wars universe.  The player's motives are very clear - find the Rebel base, or don't let the Rebel base get found.  Game play is basically commit a leader to do something - attempt a mission or move forces on the board.  Slowly the Empire will clear the 40 odd planets and begin to narrow down where the base is located, while the Rebel player desperately tries to run the clock down.

Felt a lot like War of the Ring (good) with a messier combat system (bad), but a cleaner activation system (good).  This is about twice the length of War of the Ring (bad) but still fun to play (good).  

War of the Ring is possibly the best game out there ... ever ... this is simply very good.  Like so many Fantasy Flight games, it needed more development to shave an hour off the playing time.  Someone should have told them the combat system simply needs to be faster, as all the fun is in the cards and the game of hide and seek.

RATING: 9
Explicitly amazing game, highly thematic, excellently put together, fun and interesting. Not too sure how often it will get played as it's a long (potentially very long) two player game. Though in its defence the decision space is enormous, but the core mechanisms are quite simple, you can explain the rules enough to play in about 20 minutes. Combat isn't bad, it's just not as amazing as the rest of the game, and in the end it's a bit of a roll off - which might have worked if it was a very simple one to speed up the game. These combats get very out of hand when many units are involved. That said this game for what it is offering is amazing. Let's hope ffg do something similar for game of thrones.

Addendum: this game is a recent bgg top ten entry and though cynical of more recent hotness ranking so highly, I think this games position is deserved.

RATING: 9
This game reminds me strongly of a couple other of my favorite games: Middle Earth Quest and War of the Ring.  These types of epic asymmetric games are hard to do well, but SW:R nails it.  

SW:R is clearly at its best when both players know the game well.  It is critical that both players know what their opponent is capable of.  To this end, there are some essential user-created player aids here on BGG, namely the lists of objective, mission, and action cards, as well as the battle board.

I don't understand all the complaining about the combat system.  I think it does a great job of abstracting the importance of combined arms and leadership.  The battles are exciting and usually go the way of the stronger force.  So it's not too lucky, but does allow for some surprises, and particularly can allow the Rebellion to get in some quick jabs if they bring a good leader in with their strike force.  I also love the way the Death Star is both the Empire's most deadly weapon and greatest potential liability.

RATING: 9
Lived up to the buzz.  Lots of good things in this game, but they are well-reported so I'll just nitpick a couple of things.  (1) The table sprawl is huge.   Borderline ridiculous.   (2)  The box size is silly.   Borderline ridiculous.   (3)   The opposing leader icons are a little small to see across the table.  (4) There is some nuance in when (or when NOT) to oppose missions and how to do so that the rulebook could have clarified via one good example.   The rule book and glossary are nicely done and quite clear, but lacking in enough examples and tips, which isn't essential but would have been nice at this price.

Plays quite smoothly once you get the flow of it.  Very engaging gameplay.  Combat is simple and logical.  Generates a lot of tension near the end-game, which harkens back to War Of The Ring.  Keeps me thinking about it and makes me want to play it some more, so that's a really good sign.

RATING: 7
This will be a solid 8 or 9 if expanded correctly.  Although I think it is too expensive for what it is, that does not factor into my rating.  As it stands, I think it becomes two very different games when you compare early plays to later plays and what you get out of it changes, so it's hard to rate this as I would rate other games.

In the initial game - provided you are not the type to review all components before sitting down to play - there is a lot of wonderful mystery in trying to figure out what your opponent is doing; on the flip side, if you've played it at least once on both sides, the card-limitations change the game into something else.  For example, if I recall my counts correctly, the Rebel's "stack 1" objectives amounts to four or five cards.  That's it.  With any foreknowledge of what the Rebel is attempting to do, you can pretty much prep for it before he's even ready to do it, so it becomes less a question of [i]what[/i] is the player trying to do and more about [i]when[/i] is he going to try to do it?  

Since the card pool is relatively low when it comes to the Rebel's objectives or the Empire's projects (both game-changing stacks of cards that can win the game for either player if timed correctly), the game evolves into one of anticipation and it starts looking like a magic trick whose machinations you already know.  This wouldn't be a problem if the magician is incredibly skilled as you are more taken with the execution than the actual trick, but Rebellion, while skilled, isn't an exemplary magician.  So what you get out of the game, then, depends on what you came for.

If the game you're looking for is one of cat-and-mouse - the heavily-armed Empire versus the nimble Rebellion respectively - then you will find that only in your first one or two plays, and to me, that's a little disappointing.  While thematically everything makes sense and really communicates the Star Wars universe very well, the idea of a small Rebellion exercising guerilla warfare starts to fade away as the card pool becomes known to both players.  The theme doesn't suffer in this case, so no worries there, but it becomes more like the Empire being fortune tellers and positioning themselves correctly while the Rebellion tries to find alternate ways of accomplishing what the Empire knows.  It's weird.

From a strategic standpoint, it can be an interesting talking point and it doesn't tarnish the quality of the game; only it's nature is challenged.  While you can reach this point with several other games, the reason I am being so critical about it is because the card pool is so small.  If you love a game enough, you hit this point anyway, but with a large enough card pool, the guess-work remains and the strategic choices you have are still relatively open to you.  In this case, however, you have to adjust the way you play on both sides.  The Empire [i]knows[/i] that the Rebels need 4 systems with a unit in it each.  It [i]knows[/i] that 6 systems with Rebel loyalty gets them points.  It [i]knows[/i] that leaving Coruscant open to Rebel occupation is worth two points.  The Rebellion [i]knows[/i] the Empire knows this.

So, at the end of it all, is the game good?  I like it!  lol  Despite all of that, I totally dig the way the game plays.  I know it's common-place to compare it to various games and while elements are familiar, I don't want to mislead anyone into thinking this is something it's not (it's [i]not[/i] Twilight Struggle [i]anything[/i], get that out of your head).  I can't imagine playing it as a team game; this one is 2p designed with 3-4p added as an afterthought.  The short of it is that the Rebels have a hidden base which may or may not be canonically located on Yavin (player's choice) and they need to complete several objectives in order to gain enough popular support in the galaxy to take down the Empire.  The Empire player, on the other hand, has to find this rebel base and destroy it before the rebels can have their day.  That's it.

What you get is a wonderfully asymmetric game; while the actions and overall play mechanics are the same for each side, the rebels are low on resources and easily lose systems while their missions keep them highly mobile.  On the other hand, the Empire is a formidable military beast, rolling over systems in its hunt for the rebels, but its pace is slow and it relies on capturing leaders and interrogating them.

An expansion full of objectives and projects would make this game what I want it to be, but that's not to knock on what it is.  After some plays, the challenge is different and it's still fun if somewhat predictable at that point.  YMMV.

RATING: 5
Game is way, way too long. Just too long of a game, if you like to think about your moves at all. Our group typically plays games, even the first time, within +/- 30 minutes of the printed playing time. This game, which is rated at 3-4 hours, easily takes 5-6 or more hours in a close game. Once you hit the 5 hour mark for a 2 player game, that's no longer board game territory for our play group. And while the game time does pass mostly quickly cause you're constantly doing something - there is little downtime - the sad part is that ultimately the first 1-3 turns of searching and building up don't really add much to the game, and the game could have been designed to be 50% of the current length. 

A great boardgame concept with a great setting and theme, that overall failed in execution by not aiming for a 1.5-2 playtime. 5 Stars - take it or leave it.

RATING: 9
Like many FFG games, some of the rules are too confusing, but if you can get over the fact that you will be regularly consulting the two instruction manuals, this game is incredibly fun!  It is a very different game depending on which faction you are playing.  True to A New Hope, the empire is a juggernaut that needs to expand aggressively to find the secret Rebel Base.  The Rebels feel like underdogs, but with crafty planning, can make advances toward winning.  On my first game I played as the Rebellion, and was within one turn of winning when the Empire found my base, which was unfortunately undefended.  On the second game I played as the Empire, which was able to systematically subjugate Rebel systems and capture Rebel leaders.  The Rebels feel like they are at a distinct advantage, which at first feels annoying, but the more you think about it, it is actually the way it should be.  We don't want the Rebels to be as powerful as the Empire.  We want them to win the miraculous victory.  We want Luke to make that one in a million shot down the exhaust port after all his fellow pilots have been shot down.  Thematically this game allows you to feel like you are in the world of Episodes IV - VII.

RATING: 6
[b]Sold[/b]

I really liked the hide-n-seek gameplay, and the objective cards and build queues.  I liked the idea of keeping leaders back to oppose missions, and didn't even mind the die rolls to resolve those missions - despite how much I hate "roll dice to see if you win" mechanisms.

The combat, however, was awful.  Not only was it luck-driven random dicefest nonsense, it was long and drawn out, playing over multiple rounds.  It was stopping this really interesting game of secrets and manipulation and bluffing to play a lousy mini-game.  If a second edition was released with a better combat system (maybe stolen from Cry Havoc's supper innovative approach?) I'd buy this again in a heartbeat.

RATING: 8
I like the missions you can choose to send your heroes on and a enjoyed the hunt for the rebel base, but I liked the conflict there as if heroes are completing missions they are not available to lead troops across the galaxy and subjugate another planet, thus there is a careful balance needed between the missions and expansion.

The build queue mechanic here is very clever and I like that the empire has ways to add more units to said build queue or pull then from the build queue faster than standard, and this leads to the very thematic overwhelming force for the empire, however the game is not about combat superiority. Empire must find and destroy that rebel base and the rebels must stall the empire just long enough.

A lot of mechanics here and to be honest they all seem to work well together and the result is actually quite thematic. I enjoyed this one and would like to play again, even though the rebels managed to deflect my death star laser and save Kashyyyk :shake:, and then Wedge Antillies blew up my death star :cry:... stupid Wedge!

RATING: 10
In retrospect, there was no way a game that recreates the original Star Wars trilogy wasn't going to appear in my personal top 10. This really is the quintessential SW game: it's hard to imagine it being re-themed around, say, Lord Of The Rings or Game Of Thrones. The game's mechanics feel inextricably tied to Star Wars. (Speaking of mechanics, the oft-maligned combat system is fine, if somewhat clumsy. And you should feel free to use the action cards in your first game, despite what the rules say to do.) A true narrative emerges during this game: as much as I'm trying to win, it's just as much fun to see what happens next.

I'd say the Rebels have a much more uphill battle, which is the way it should be. I don't want to play a perfectly balanced Star Wars game. However, the Imperials have a much steeper learning curve. Familiarity with the Objective deck is important for both sides, as the Imperial player can doom themselves by being reckless.

The game also feels complete out of the box. I've got the expansion now and I'm super excited to eventually play with it, but you shouldn't feel the need to rush out and buy it at the same time as the base game. There's plenty of Leaders, Missions, etc. to keep the game fresh for a very long time.

RATING: 9
SW: Rebellion really plays differently than you would think when looking at all the pieces before playing. You would think this is an Axis & Allies-type game, but it actually shares little with dice-chucking Ameritrash games. I found it actually had a lot more in common with Twilight Struggle. Players are attempting to enact various missions on the board to either bolster their plans or muck up their opponents, and complete objectives to win reputation or build projects to turn the tide of war. With the right amount of influence played into these various systems, the better chance of these missions being completed. Opponents must balance whether to assign their leaders to their own plans, or hold back to confront their opponent's plans later on or to keep their leaders for movement.  Rebellion is gloriously asymmetrical.  The rules are brief and straightforward, with most of the complexity downloaded to the card effects.  The theme shines through!  While combat might run on autopilot as it happens, I do find it rewards good planning and also allows for some surprises.  Once you play it a couple of times, the Combat system will flow better and not bog down the game.  And for what it's worth, the Empire is purposely designed to overpower the Rebels in firepower, so sometimes just starting a battle feels like a foregone conclusion (that conclusion typically being a win for the Empire).  But as we know, if the Empire concentrates so much firepower on one pocket of the universe, a lone X-Wing might be able to sneak in and show them who actually has the upper hand.  The production is pretty top-notch, other than the usual FFG oversight of a decent insert. I'd still say it's about $30 overpriced, but if you're a Star Wars fan and Corey Konieczka fan, and trust the boys and girls at FFG to not skimp, then this is probably an auto-buy at any price.  If anything detracts other than the price, it is long (4-5 hours) and exhausting (in a positive "I just ran a marathon" sort of way) but if you have the time and endurance, there are few more rewarding experiences in gaming than winning at Rebellion.  It also (like Twilight Struggle) slightly benefits the player who has played more than the other and has a better recall of the cards in their opponent's deck and their own deck and is able to plan for possibilities. But I'd ignore that fact and try to play with all the excitement of not knowing what is going to come up (but just know that will make thematic sense and surprise you rather than frustrate you).

RATING: 10
This isn't my attempt at an "objective" review.

But this is my absolute favorite game!

I enjoy games of all kinds: I love euros, and Ameritrash, cooperative and competitive, party games and big chunky games.

This is one big chunky Ameritrash game with a healthy dose of Euro.

I can't even explain why I love it so much, but I love this game.  I always want to play it!  However, I don't always have the time - which is perhaps part of the allure.

There is no getting around the fact that this is a long game.  I have played this game 7 or 8 times now and it clocks in around 5 hours for me and I don't see it getting shorter than that, realistically.  This game is an event, and boy does it deliver.

One of the reasons the game takes a while is the fact that there is so much to think about.  It's interesting how asymmetrical this game yet you still feel like you are playing the same game, not two separate games.

The almost worker-placement of the game provides a nice euro engine that drives the Ameritrash madness.  If you are the imperial player you are playing a very chunky resource management game that I find absolutely addictive!  

The rebels will win or lose based on how they fly by the seat of their pants and make daring raids and hit-and-run, hamstringing the massive resource machine that is the empire.  It really feels like the movies come to life.  It's swingy, but your defeat or victory is based on your decisions, gambles, and mistakes.

It doesn't hurt that I am a big Star Wars fan!  I am not even trying to say that this is the best game I own, but it is the one I like the best, if that makes sense to anyone else but me.

RATING: 7
I just find the base mechanic (deploying and using characters) very uninspired and boring.  Add to that the strictly two-player , the length, the overly large box, and the "so, you've found me?  I'll just move somewhere else, try again" aspects and I'll find a game that I'm not interested in at all.

And second: I've only played as the Rebels, and in general I loathe playing reactively. Maybe if I played as the Empire, I'll rate this a point or two better.

Ratings on BGG Scale:
"likely won’t play this again" (3)
"Mediocre" (5)

RATING: 8
El sabor de la trilogía original -verdadera y única- está muy presente en este estupendo juego. Llama la atención su mecánica central: los jugadores disponen de diversos personajes y cada turno los utilizan para mover unidades por la Galaxia, atacar al enemigo, cumplir misiones, o bien tratar de impedir que el enemigo cumpla las suyas.

El Imperio trata de localizar y destruir la base secreta rebelde, mientras la Rebelión intenta sobrevivir y acelerar el fin de la partida.

Se trata ante todo de un juego muy divertido y dinámico, que lógicamente disfrutarán más los fans de Star Wars. Las batallas épicas se combinan estupendamente con las aventuras y acciones protagonizadas por los personajes que aparecen en las películas.

RATING: 6
Looks beautiful.  I can't wait to play it. 

1) Kind of not what I thought it would be.  I need more plays to really know, but this seems like a alternative version of Twilight Struggle, and I hate that game. 

2) A couple of plays and this game is a huge time commitment (3-4+ hours), and then it will end suddenly on you.  That sucks. 

3) Played again only due to the wonderful theme, and again the game ended suddenly.  That stinks.

So, this game is hammer and nail with fleet-- meaning Rebels will almost never win a straight up fight, so this is no war game.

It is all cat and mouse for 3+ hours. Then, when the rebels actually win, will win suddenly after 4 hours of play.  The rebel victories do not feel thematic to me at all. 

Ultimately, rebels are all missions with minimal fleet.  The Empire should be a great deal of fleet with minimal missions.

This is a card advantage game disguised as a Star Wars War Game, which it is certainly not.

RATING: 9.4
There is little I can say about Star Wars: Rebellion that hasn't been said before. The game is amazing, no doubt about that, but perhaps I can shed a bit of a unique perspective. I've been in the hobby about three years now and my tastes have certainly solidified over time. I like euros, euros with theme, but euros nonetheless. The only "dudes on a map" games I own are Cry Havoc and Blood Rage and even those are euros in ameritrash clothing (and they happen to be among the least played games in my collection). I tried Mansions of Madness. I wanted to love it. But in the end I rated it a 5.5 and sold it from my collection. Games like Star Wars Rebellion are ones I typically do NOT enjoy.

Yet I think when all is said and done, SW:R could go down as my favorite game of all-time. The game is flat-out incredible. Fantasy Flight nailed the theme here. What makes the game so great are the mission cards and how they tie back to the movies so well. You can run a mission using Luke and Yoda to Dahobah and if successful, turn Luke into a Jedi. But at the time, in one of my games, Luke was already captured by the dark side, so that mission was not worth it for me. Perhaps I should send Leia on a rescue mission? There is nothing in board gaming that I have experienced to date that makes me feel like I am IN a world like this game does. I liked it so much that I played it again three days later with a different opponent. Each game played out much differently with the Empire winning easily in my first play and the Rebellion surviving in the second. The only thing that could break this game for me is if I determine that the sides are imbalanced. One of my friends has played this 5x so far and said that in his plays, the Empire has never won. If that turns out to be true, that will be a shame, but I will say this. I am very happy to keep playing to find out. This game is a wonder, a joy, an EXPERIENCE. You owe it to yourself as a gamer to play it.

Oh, and when you do? Make sure you stream the Star Wars soundtrack (free if you have an Amazon Prime subscription using the Amazon Music app). It creates a great atmosphere and backdrop for your plays!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've taught this game to gamers and non-gamers alike. It's great and the components are stellar. One of the most played games in my collection.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Impressive. :D
I believe this is a lighter version of the War of the Ring, while the combat system is definitely better. Don't believe the criticism about the supposed clunkiness of the combat system. I found it pretty neat even for bigger engagements. 

In my first game as the Imperial I concentrated too much on military conquest and Imperial Diplomacy, in order to consolidate my power, augment my production and destroy Rebel insurgents. I have fallen short by not  devoting energies into espionage and therefore I wasn't able to find the Rebel base till the bitter end. I had fun nevertheless so I'd consider that a good 4 hours long experience. That time really passed fast.

In the second game, as the Imperial, I devoted most of my attention to discover the enemy base. By turn 5-6 I had a fair good idea of where it was, I attacked it earlier and was lucky with a land mission which makes possible to attack systems from a distance. There was little the Rebel could do by then. He resisted the first attack, but could do nothing for the subsequent one, which was overwhelming. All in all a good game, but I don't know honestly what the Rebel could have done to advert the Imperial onslaught.

Again a 4 hours long game for my third game. As the Rebels which I played for the first time times couldn't be tougher. Matteo, my host, was very careful in not letting me get any points, and indeed it was extremely difficult. I just got one by sacrificing Obi-Wan, and destroying - at great cost - an imperial star destroyer. I was able, later in the game, to collect some points conquering Coruscant with a double mission. A very lucky thing which I don't think Matteo will allow me to pull off in other games. 
In the meanwhile my leaders were captured one after the other, and Leila was turned to the dark side. By this time I was feeling pretty claustrophobic, and I had nowhere to run, my forces basically only present in the base. The base was then suddenly attacked, but fortunately I was able to repel this attack, which, everything considered, could have given me the game. Next turn the imperial forces could have gotten the base, but it was a 50% chance. In any case, before their attack, I resolved a mission with the Consul and Luke - which had become a Jedi. That mission was to attack a local planet which was subjugated, a 3 troopers against 3 stormtroopers. Emperor Palpatine tried to block the plot, fortunately to no avail, and a battle ensued, but Luke's ability and rerolling dice carried the day. With that I scored the last point in order to win the game. Thematically Palpatine trying to convert Luke was slayed and the Empire liberated of his influence for ever. Great, good and very tense game, till the end!
