=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I love Star Wars. Love it. Have since I was a kid. Everyone said this game was Star wars in a box, and it really is. It really captures the feel of the movies, the feeling of helplessness of the rebels as they try to stay hidden and out of reach of the Empire, while simultaneously striking at them to hamper their progress and gain support throughout the galaxy. Sending out your heroes to complete missions or lead your fleets. Playing this game felt like playing an alternate version of the movies.

The catch is, I don't feel like that makes for a very good game. In the movies there are many situations where blind luck or circumstance drastically changes the way things go. Obviously in the movies these situations ultimately play out in the rebels favour. The game has done a good job of translating those kind of situations through the use of card play and dice rolling, but for a game that usually clocks in at 3+ hours, I feel like it is ultimately unsatisfying to have the result so dependent on these moments of luck. What works in the movies makes for a frustrating experience in the game. The gameplay equivalent of Han stepping on a twig and setting in motion the events that lead to the Ewoks joining them and helping get the shield down vs him not stepping on the twig and things ending in likely doom for the rebellion does not make a satisfying conclusion to the game as far as I'm concerned.

So, ultimately, this is a game I really want to like, but that I just can't. If I want a Star Wars experience, I recommend watching the movies.

I'm forced to drop the rating to a 7.5 instead of an 8.5.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Yera, y tambien D.A

El gran juego definitivo de Star Wars del año (en este caso, del 2016) :D

Este es un 4X (ya sabeis... expansion, exterminacion, etc). En castellano: dominacion, combate contra el enemigo y conquista. Es 1vs1 (aunque se puede jugar en equipos de dos) y asimetrico. cada bando (imperio y rebelion) tiene sus propios objetivos y varias rutinas de juego propias. 

El objetivo del imperio es localizar, cercar y exterminar la base rebelde, y el objetivo de la rebelion es "aumentar su reputacion" cumplimentando diversas misiones "anti-imperio". si el imperio localiza la base y la destruye: gana. si la rebelion consigue aumentar su reputacion hasta el punto de coincidir con el marcador de tiempo del juego y lo hace antes de que los imperiales localicen y destruyan su base, entonces ganan la partida. 

Todo ello por supuesto amenizado con epicas batallas estelares (bueno, no son tan epicas, pero dan un buen nivel en el genero) y un festival del plastico: destructores y superdestructores imperiales, cazas de ambos bandos, e incluso tres estrellas de la muerte, una de ellas "incompleta" igualito que en la pelicula. Un puntazo. 

El juego basicamente representa el arco de las tres peliculas originales. y lo hace bastante bien. no es del todo teledirigido y cada bando tiene cierta libertad de accion dentro del guion establecido. la jugabilidad es variada... ¿que puede salir mal? 

En mi opinion donde falla un poco es en la movilidad de las flotas imperiales. se mueven como flotas de barcos. muuuuuyyy despaaaacio, de un sector al siguiente. es mas estrategico y le da un puntillo de facilidad al jugador de la rebelion... pero en mi opinion no es realista. me parece logico que el juego "obligue" al jugador imperial a tener varias "flotas" y le impida moverlas como le salga del pitoto (incluido "fusionarlas"), pero que una flota requiera 2, 3 o mas turnos para llegar a un determinado sistema porque se mueven como tortugas artriticas por el mapa me parece sinceramente un cachondeo. hay alguna carta "cheta" que permite saltarse esto (moverse a un sector cualquiera como si estuviera adyacente). pero eso en mi opinion deberia ser una opcion de movimiento, no una carta cheta. 

En fin, dejando aparte el "rage". es un gran juego y por supuesto, merece mas partidas para valorarlo adecuadamente :)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
7/8/16: First play-through ended fantastically. The first four turns were pretty rough, especially considering my cousin and I (both seasoned gamers) had read both manuals and watched a few videos prior to playing. The different card types (and their lack of deck title or symbol on the back of the cards) threw us for a loop paired with questions about resolving the turn phases.

The manuals included (How to Play and Rules Glossary) really left a bit to be desired, namely that there was no two-page spread simply showing turn order and/or starting components. We found that when questions arose we had to read both manuals me piece together the information to get the answer.

Aside from that slight annoyance once we got the hang of it the game played beautifully. It's fun as hell and we spent the hour after I lost talking about the cool shit we just did.

RATING: 8
Okay, so this is only based on one play. I was not "blown away" by the game, but I think this needs repeated play to be properly assessed. I will say this - I felt a lot of pressure as the Rebels. The game swung violently when the Imperials captured and released Leia with a homing beacon - because of fortuitous probe deck draws, the Imperial knew almost exactly where my base was. 

I liked it, it was very tense. It definitely has that Twilight Struggle of feeling of damage mitigation, at least from the Rebel side. 

I will also admit that my experience may have been somewhat hampered by poor play on my part. I was really focused on getting planets that would help me build more units originally. Admittedly, it is unwise for rebels to even attempt an arms race with the Empire. Instead, they seem to need to focus on specific objectives and misleading the Imperials.

This is a tentative 7.5 with the possibility of going as far as a 10. I think I will enjoy being the Imperial player more, so once I get a chance to do that, I will update my rating!

Edit 1: Have played a second time now, although we didnt quite finish. I can safely say that it is more difficult to play the Rebel side, mostly because those objectives are just hard to actually complete! Rating now an 8 because I am thinking about potential strategies for this game after playing and in between plays.

RATING: 9.26
If you like Star Wars you will love this game.  Only knock on the game is that it will take you about 3 hours to play once you have all the rules memorized.

Our first play through took 6 hours because we constantly checked the rule book for various things.  We didn't even realize we had been playing for 6 hours though.

The game is dripping with Theme, has all the characters you know from Episodes 4, 5, and 6, and has defining moments you will recognize.  

The best part of this game is how you can rewrite Star Wars lore and have stories to reminisce about.  For instance, in our game Obi Wan got captures, put in carbonite, led the Imperials to our secret base at Tattooine.  The Rebels were able to narrowly escape to establish a new base on Dantooine.  Later Princess Leia got captured and was rescued by Obi Wan, who, was again captured on a future mission.  The Rebels finally were able to curry enough support from the galaxy by destroying a Death Star that was underconstruction in the Dantooine system.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.2
Gorgeous components. I'm in love!
A really strategic game with its very unique "leaders assignment & reveal" mechanic to "hint" at what actions a player plans to take in a turn, forcing to plan your full turn in advance, and yet try to adapt just a little bit.
Full of the tension that would have inhabited both factions, one thriving to just stay alive and hidden, the other one desperately trying to find the base and crush the insurrection. Not to mention - plenty of true-to-heart Star Wars moments.
It really takes a long time to play. But it really is a blast.
I just wish combats didn't have so much randomness (dice + tactics drawing - the tactics part is addressed in the expansion). Mission resolution also really uses a lot of dice, which feels only half OK. I guess it is what makes this game "sort of a little lighter", compared to what would be a purely strategic game.
I wonder if a no-dice variant could work...

RATING: 8
Nice area-movement adaptation of the almost 20-year-old strategic computer game set during the original Star Wars trilogy.  Unlike the computer game, the sides are nicely asymmetric, with the Rebels hopelessly outmatched in the military contest overall but with some nice opportunities to create local superiorities and deliver setbacks to the Empire.  Combat is aided by an interesting system that simply captures differences between troops and vehicles on the ground and fighters and capital ships in space.  The overall game experience is also enhanced by some truly excellent production values.
This is, however, a Star Wars themed game, not a game about Star Wars.  The characters are familiar, but don’t expect them to behave in familiar ways.  Characters that you would expect to work together (like Han and Chewbacca) will operate on their own, and there is no difference between force-sensitive characters and others, a key omission from Lucas’ creation.  The worst offender here though, and the one that takes me out of the Star Wars feel of the game, is the movement pace.  With the exception of leaders and a few missions, units are limited to a sluggish pace of one area per turn.  I was really disappointed by the lack of a hyperspace rule.  The general construct of the game itself also creates narrative problems.  The overwhelming military advantage of the Empire means that either a similar advantage needs to go to the Rebels on the diplomatic side, or a time limit needs to be applied.  The latter was chosen.  The objective of the game is therefore for the Imperials to find the hidden Rebel base before time runs out.  It’s Clue meets Battleship with a time pressure on the Empire in a manner that does not seem consistent with the movies.
Overall, this is a good game, and it’s amazing that it has taken more than three decades for somebody to do this.  I had hoped for more of a “simulation” of Lucas’ galaxy, and created a variant to make the game closer to what I was hoping to see.  But it’s a fine game as is if you’re not too picky about the narrative details.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Only played once (as Rebels), and I enjoy the SW universe. I played a partial game (~2.5 hours) and got to blow up the death star, so that was great! Interesting asymmetry, though I'm not sure it feels exactly right that all the rebels need to do is hide their base. In War of the Ring (another epic, asymmetric game), it really does feel right that all the world can be war-torn, as long as the ring is destroyed. But in this, it doesn't feel right that everyone can get annihilated, planets destroyed and subjugated, but as long as the rebel base hasn't been found yet, the rebels win when the timer is up. That's not actually the right win condition - it should be blowing up the death star twice, or defeating the emperor, or something like that. I could imagine that nearly the whole galaxy could be controlled by the dark side, but once the emperor is killed, the rebels win. Or once the death star is destroyed again, the rebels win. But simply staying hidden long enough... nope. So the whole game feels wrong, since the win condition is wrong.

RATING: 9.5
I do not rate the game as 10 because I am still waiting for the perfect game, but this one is very close to perfection. 
It is absolutely thematic, the system is asymetric but perfectly balanced, replayable, it is an epic game with plenty of different valid strategies. You do not need to do always the same thing, many paths can take you to victory.
If I have to say a couple of possible improvements, I would say that the battles may become a bit messy if you start a dealing cards frenzy. I have not played the expansion system. The other issue is, more than in other games, a new player needs 2 to 3 games before being really competitive, you need to know what type of cards the other player may have. There are some combos that, well played without the other player being prepared, can kill the game. 
But, even when you are defeated you enjoy the game. If you like this kind of complete and highly strategic games, you have to try this one.

RATING: 6
Ambitious and decent design, but:

1. you need dedicated players to play this game (this narrows down the opportunities for regular play significantly)

2. there are too many options  - absolutely splendid as far as flavour of the game is concerned, but if you play optimally (or just rationally) you just won't be using them.  Why on earth (as the Empire) develop terrifying technologies (like Super Star Destroyer) or annihilate systems with Death Star when you should focus just on moving your units and searching for the rebel base.  The Rebels likewise - why bother with Sabotage mission for example when the Empire will have enough of production anyway (removing the sabotage marker sporadically),  
There are so many options for both sides and that is great, epic, immersive and all dandy, but they turn out to be just unneccessary decorations if you play SW:R competitively.  This is especially troubling in case of the Empire which should ignore its missions to great degree and focus on searching the galaxy for rebel base.  The military advantage will be there no matter what...

Still, I love plenty of ideas implemented in the design and that's why I can play the game not only without much fuss, but even with pleasure :) (assuming _someone_ would have and bring a copy).

The epic, thematic, large-scale, choke-full of miniatures Star Wars game I have awaited for all my life. It is a very fun game, with many hard decisions. Sadly, the game is not perfect, it runs a tad too long, perhaps, and the common complain that the combat is bland or boring is pretty justified, especially concerning the combat cards. They hurt especially since the theme is so strong in this one and they can come off as dissonant.

***UPDATE***
This game has real staying power, and is surely Corey K.'s masterwork. Once you accept the minor flaws and idiosyncracies, the game unveils itself as rich, dense, complex and exciting. A true challenger to War of the Rings' throne of "saga in a box". Up to 9!

RATING: 7
2016-08-29

Initial Rating: 7.0 (August 2016)

I was a fan of Star Wars right up until the last movie (The Force Awakens which I despise but that’s other topic :D) but I still have fond memories of the books, the PC game and previous movies. Besides, Star Wars: Rebellion is a game well regarded here on BGG so I was keen to play it.

As is usual from FFG, the game components are outstanding, the miniatures are very detailed and they look great on the board. The art is very good as well.

The theme is great as I love the original trilogy.

The game´s rules aren’t very complex, but there are many rules. You can explain them under 20 minutes. Both rulebooks seem intimidating at first, but they are far easier to understand than I initially expected. Gameplay is around 3 and a half hours.

The decisions needed to play the game aren’t trivial, but aren’t that hard either. As the Empire you have to move your armies through the galaxy looking for the Rebel base. As the Rebel player you have to hide your base as best as you can. Both players have to decide which mission to accomplish and whose leaders to assign (or oppose) to each mission (that’s the best part of the game). I also enjoy the cat and mouse dynamics between the factions. The Galactic Empire is very powerful military wise while the Rebel Alliance has very meager resources. In my game, the Rebel Alliance didn’t win a lot of combats but almost win the game nonetheless. Combat isn’t as important as I initially thought. Star Wars: Rebellion is a deception game.

The feeling of playing and controlling both Death Stars is amazing!, it has an epic feel to it :D.

Combat is ok and easy to understand. There is some luck with the dice, but most of the time the expected result happens, that is, I don’t feel the game has a lot of uncontrollable luck, you can prepare for it. There is much more uncontrollable luck with the cards (missions, projects, tactics).

To me, Star Wars: Rebellion is only a two player game, with more players the game slows down and the downtime increases to unmanageable levels. 

On the bad side, from my very limited perspective, it seems winning with the Rebel Alliance is much easier than with the Galactic Empire due to a mission card that the rebel player always has at hand (the one that lets him move his base to 4 or up to 8 different systems if you use two leaders). I need more plays to verify this claim, but if true, that could hamper my desire to play the game many times. It seems playing with the Empire requires a lot of finesse while playing with the Rebel alliance is easy and straightforward. I like asymmetric games, but so far, it seems to me both factions aren’t balanced. I need more plays to see if this is an issue for me or not. The rebel victory doesn’t feel very thematic, they can get away with lots of mistakes and, as moving the ships through the galaxy is so slow, time is on their side.

Bottom line, Star Wars: Rebellion is a good Ameritrash game. These days I no longer enjoy that genre as much as before but I enjoyed the game. For now, it is a borderline 7.0 to me and I have not yet decided if I should keep it in my game collection or not. I need more plays to see if the rebels can escape as easily as they did in our game. I want to play it again soon. Much better than War of the Ring though.

Current Rating: 7.0

RATING: 9
This is the Star Wars game you're looking for! The various elements of the game work together elegantly, resulting in thematic gameplay that captures the feel of the original trilogy brilliantly. Smooth mechanics and an accessible, intuitive ruleset provide an excellent framework to deliver this exquisite experience. The cat-and-mouse chase emulates the Empire's struggle to locate the Rebels, and the disparity in military power between the two sides reflects the situation in the films. The missions, objectives, and projects provide layers of strategic elements: deciding when to attempt missions, whom to send on them, the order in which to execute them, whether to oppose your opponent's mission (and with whom), etc. These cards fuel the story of the game as each side strives to gain the upper hand. The combat system is simple and fast without being rudimentary, and the tactic cards give both players some tricks up their sleeves. The innovative building mechanics necessitate precise planning and make certain systems advantageous to control at key moments. The variety of leaders and their various abilities are yet another way that the theme and essence of the Star Wars universe shines through. Add to all of this the superb production value of the components and you have the quintessential Star Wars game on your hands. This game is the ultimate power in the Star Wars universe, and fear of this technological terror will keep all other Star Wars games in line.

RATING: 8.5
I really like the arc to the game - how the leaders gradually increase so you are getting more and more missions and activations done as the game progresses.  Also, how the rebel objectives become worth more points as the game progresses and the empire gets closer to finding the rebel base.  The whole thing is nicely thought out - like, with rapid mobilization, it protects against the Empire accidentally stumbling upon the rebel base early on.  Rapid mobilization becomes less effective the longer the game goes on, but it doesn't matter as much becomes the game has developed sufficiently anyway and the rebels have had time to become competitive.  The whole theme is very well implemented, with the overpowering empire, and the rebels doing hit-and-runs and sabotage here and there.

Notes from 2nd play: 
Love the game of Cat-and-Mouse, and from the rebels side, balancing objectives with hiding the base and with building the units you need.  Also, the map is really brilliant - the non-adjacency areas are really effective at suggesting a 3-D galaxy area on a 2-D board.

RATING: 10
Currently my favourite game, you're basically in the co-directors chair re-telling the Original Triology with your opponent. Behind the theme there is a solid, asymetric game with a lot of depth which only shines through on repeated play. It does requires a large investment of time (& willing opponent) to learn & occasional play to stop you getting rusty. The hardest part is finding other plays who are as entheusiatic about it as myself! My least favorite part is the combat, which uses card randomness to add to dice randomness.

Overall (with two experienced players) both sides feel like they are loosing for the duration of the game, instead it's that rare beast, a truly balanced game where randomness plays little part. My worst game was one where I drew good cards, had a good position, strong builds, but wasted it all through poor strategy. Conversely I've won games where all the dice gods seemed against me, and both leader & card draws were poor.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Excellent game that makes you feel more immersed in the Star Wars galaxy than most video games even.  What I love most about this game isn't just the fact that it is a Star Wars map painter; it's its wonderful asymmetrical gameplay which makes playing as the Empire and the Rebellion feel unique and distinct from one another with their own unique challenges.  

The Rebellion is entirely objective oriented as you have to achieve very specific goals in order to increase your reputation and bring the galaxy that much closer to freedom.  This can lead to some wonderful mission planning as you try to maximize your moves and heroes to achieve the most objectives per turn.  One particular play that stands out in my mind was one turn where I had Chewbacca lead a strike team from the Rebel base to a world occupied by the Empire.  I won the fight, thus lifting the occupation.  The next mission I played then allowed for me to safely return all of the ground forces back to the Rebel Base.  It was like my strike team was never there - a true hit and run mission.  At the end of the round, I got two objective points: one for lifting an occupation and another for winning a ground combat that round.  These are the most satisfying moments when playing as the Rebellion.  The moments where everything aligns to hit the Empire just right and advance your reputation towards victory.  Then the other half of your game is focused around throwing the Imperial player off your trail through misdirects and a good poker face when there are Star Destroyers the next system over.  

The Empire plays almost like a detective game of some sort.  Losing Stormtroopers and Tie fighters doesn't matter to the Empire, only finding and destroying the Rebel Base.  Everything the Empire does, whether that be capturing and interrogating enemy heroes or spreading your forces to occupy regions of space, is geared towards finding and eliminating the Rebel base.  In this way, playing as the Empire almost feels tenser than playing as the Rebellion as the turns fly by and your desperate search continues.  Though you have the superior numbers, you have to be spread out unlike the Rebel Alliance which can attack with its full force at seemingly any place and anytime.  However, nothing is sweeter than sleuthing your way to figure out the Rebel player's location and bringing down the might of the Empire upon them.

Another aspect that really makes this game shine above others of its type is the previously mentioned mission card system which allows you to lovingly recreate scenarios from the films or craft unique adventures of your own.  From a diplomatic battle of wits between Princess Leia and Grand Moff Tarkin or the Emperor trying to turn a captured Luke Skywalker to the dark side, you really can forge your own Star Wars story.  These actions of subterfuge and tactics will really stick with you long after the generic battles of other games are forgotten and the characters go a long way to help that.  I'll never forget the time that I lost the game as the Empire when the Emperor was killed by Luke Skywalker in the Battle of Mygeeto where the Rebel Base was located in the last turn of the game.  My friend used the Return of the Jedi objective card to end the game in the grandest fashion possible, and, even though I was on the losing side, it speaks volumes that a loss in this game was more fun and memorable than a victory in many other games.  Star Wars Rebellion will always hold a treasured place in my collection.

RATING: 9
After four plays, I'm satisfied with dubbing this a very enjoyable asymmetric game.  The Rebels' strategy is not one of confrontation, but of delay, and they have a surprisingly ability to come back from a weakened position.  Overall complexity is quite low for an FFG game, with most of the rules & flavor being snuck into the Mission Card deck.  I really like the black/red dice distinction in combat (which optimizes most units to fight their own class) and thought it the right mix of dice and card accents.  The whole package feels lovingly crafted and clever, which is just how I like my games.

RATING: 7
One of the few FFG big box games I could imagine owning myself at some time. It's a good mix between strategic look-ahead and tactical optimization. While featuring dice, choosing the times when to use them in combat or on a mission is more decisive than the luck involved in the outcome. The theme is well-implemented and contributes to my enjoyment. A rare case as usually theme in this type of game is used to cover insubstantial mechanism. Star Wars: Rebellion is different. Decisions matter, clever hand management and an action plan where to assign leaders each round are of importance. The only thing where the game can break down is a premature lucky discovery of the rebel base, which, while thematically appropriate, can force the rebel player into a defensive mode where resources needed for buildup have to be burnt for escape if at all possible.

RATING: 8
I've played three games of this so far with three different people. Each game has come down to a situation where both players were close or relatively close to winning. In my third game, for example, the Imperials, discovering the Rebel base with a more substantial force than that defending the base but who had to win that turn (to avoid losing to the time and reputation markers meeting in the refresh phase), lost because the Rebels had the plans to destroy the Death Star, blew it up, and got the two objective points needed to finish the game instantly. I'm guessing this last-minute thing will reduce somewhat if/once we gain more experience and move to a free setup. Everything about the production is good except for the plastic bases that chew into the cardboard leader standees. The combat is maybe not as bad as you've heard, but it's not great; even after having played the game three times, I still have to look at the combat sequence, the experience is not all that fluid, and you kind of just want it to be over. My one real wish for an expansion is a dice-only combat variant in which the foundation is either different ships have different to-hit numbers on the same die (say, a d10), as in Twilight Imperium III, or there's a static to-hit number and different ships have different die "sizes" (d6, d8, d10, etc.), as in Dungeons and Dragons Conquest of Nerath (and probably many others).

RATING: 6
A game of one-sided Stratego where one player is knocking down pegs in a dwindling array hoping to hit the flag. The plastic components, the attractive board, the characters and their abilities and affinity with various events all contribute to a sense of grand scope where elements from the films are organically mixed and remixed as you play. It also helps (and hurts) that both sides are constantly fighting (and gaming) inertia in terms of production and movement. The rebel player needs to stay on a curve of systems held and ships owned in order to accelerate time and gain more ships. The imperial player needs to disrupt this curve and draw the right probe cards to reach the point where pure stomping is all that's needed. Downsides: playing time (could take six hours, could end at any time), multiple sources of randomness that add up rather than even out.

RATING: 9

Rebellion is a terrific and Epic Struggle for control of the Star Wars galaxy. Simple and thematic play from round to round, each side maneuvers and schemes to achieve its specific goals.  Combat can be clunky at times and epic battles become Dice chuckers (Then again so was RISK and we ALL used to love that). A huge table hog, it's worth the time and space it takes to play the game, especially when on your last turn as the Empire is about to destroy your base (its goal) you run a mission that sends Luke Skywalker on a run to destroy the Death Star, and with a die roll and a well played card, you get enough point to secure a Rebel Alliance victory. RATING: 7
Good game, but a bit too long with four players.
Our first game (with default setup and without action cards) took probably about 5 hours in addition to maybe 1 hour of explanation.

A disadvantage of playing with four players is the fact that the amount of leaders per player can become lopsided. As the Rebellion Admiral I only got Ackbar, while for the General we chose Chewie (we needed his skill for several missions), then Luke (obvious, since we had the Dagobah mission), and the last recruit was no choice at all, because we drew Luke (again) and Obi-Wan.
The Imperials also had 3 Admiral leaders and 5 for the General, and picked those because of their set of missions.
I'm not sure if the missions are generally designed more for the General leaders or if it was by chance of drawing the missions.

I wouldn't call the combat system bad, but it was more tedious than I wished. The tactics cards are an interesting idea, unforunately they were often useless in the specific situation.

Building units was also a bit frustrating for the Rebellion. We didn't manage to build strong units in the beginning (we lost Utapau before we could use it), then managed to field one Mon Calamari cruiser late in the game and put two further ones in the pipeline in the same turn through the use of two missions on Mon Calamari, but those weren't ready before the game was over. We could have even put another cruiser in the pipeline, but the Rebellion only has three available.
The Empire started production of a second Death Star as well as a SSD, but both weren't ready before the game ended (at the end of turn 8).
{CHMM}

RATING: 5
This game has so much potential, and I can tell why people like it, but so many things about it turn me, personally, away from it. If you think you will like it, you almost certainly WILL, don't let anything I say prevent you from buying it, but it just makes me not want to play it.
The combat feels like a drag whenever it happens. The rules for it feel like they needed to have some combat mechanic and they made the most ridiculous system imaginable. It is both slow and clunky, AND offers no decisions to either side! Random, but makes you have to carry everything out anyway.
Every single action you can do in this game can be denied by a single roll. I usually make the argument of luck averaging out throughout the game, but in this game some crucial actions that need to happen for the game to continue or end, all come down to one or a few rolls.
The cards you get all reference the movies... but a bit too much. There is no room for imagination when every card is literally just a scene from a movie. It feels like the game is asking you to imagine this galaxy with all these planets and telling you that you can have your own version of it... but you end up just following the events of the movies, at random orders, in random places, with random people.
The idea of the game is so good! Hide and seek, good theme, big setting, gorgeous components... but the mechanics of it all fall flat.

RATING: N/A
Star Wars: Rebellion is a board game of epic conflict between the Galactic Empire and Rebel Alliance for two to four players!

Experience the Galactic Civil War like never before. In Rebellion, you control the entire Galactic Empire or the fledgling Rebel Alliance. You must command starships, account for troop movements, and rally systems to your cause. Given the differences between the Empire and Rebel Alliance, each side has different win conditions, and you'll need to adjust your play style depending on who you represent:

As the Imperial player, you can command legions of Stormtroopers, swarms of TIEs, Star Destroyers, and even the Death Star. You rule the galaxy by fear, relying on the power of your massive military to enforce your will. To win the game, you need to snuff out the budding Rebel Alliance by finding its base and obliterating it. Along the way, you can subjugate worlds or even destroy them.
As the Rebel player, you can command dozens of troopers, T-47 airspeeders, Corellian corvettes, and fighter squadrons. 

However, these forces are no match for the Imperial military. In terms of raw strength, you'll find yourself clearly overmatched from the very outset, so you'll need to rally the planets to join your cause and execute targeted military strikes to sabotage Imperial build yards and steal valuable intelligence. To win the Galactic Civil War, you'll need to sway the galaxy's citizens to your cause. If you survive long enough and strengthen your reputation, you inspire the galaxy to a full-scale revolt, and you win.

RATING: 7.5
Asymmetrical Twilight Struggle-type two player game with unique game mechanics, creativity, and excellent aesthetic design and component quality. Impressed by the balance considering the extent of the asymmetry here. 

Although this prominently features some Ameritrash game mechanics i normally hate: dice rolling, rewarding decks of unique 'event' type cards, with the right mindset (and while watching the trilogy in the background), I found this to be a fun, but deep casual game experience. Just need the right mindset - for any dice-rolling ameritrash game, theme comes first. Can't be overly-competitive. 

Gf liked the theme but found the rules, numerous rule exceptions, and the sheer number of possible strategies and actions to be overwhelming and unfun.

RATING: 8
[u]Comments:[/u]
What a fantastic strategic game this is. Don't let the price point, or the number of pieces and the rulebook intimidate you. What you will find in this box is pure gaming genius and very approachable right from the get go. I have come to love the FFG model of having two instruction booklets that lets you get setup and playing quickly with adding rules that you may need during game play in the extended rulebook. This will definitely come in handy while playing your first couple of games of this. The mechanics of the game are really straightforward, and allow for two different gaming experiences depending on which side of the table you are playing on. The Empire is trying to destroy the Rebels utterly by finding their hidden base and wiping them off the mat, using a Death Star or two if need be. The Rebel player on the other hand is just trying to last long enough to draw enough sympathy to their cause to overthrow the Empire. Its a cat and mouse game wrapped in a Star Wars theme draped in awesomeness. I just wish they would have inlcluded enough minis that I didn't have to buy a second set of the game to play [gameid=3548] with miniatures instead of standees.

RATING: 8
Very good two player light wargame with some elements borrowed from the Scotland Yard genre of hide and seek games, relatively simple combat somewhat in the Axis and Allies style, a little bit of Twilight Struggle area control/card management and some unique resource allocation elements of its own.  It also manages to incorporate this medley of mechanics into the framework of a fairly thematic game with a lot of neat touches from the Star Wars franchise. My only slight gripe is that the tactic cards slow down the combat (in a fairly long game) and make it significantly more fiddly although they do add tension.

RATING: 7
The Assignment turn of each player, where we choose Missions, can be too long (10 missions at a time). 

The game play is more tactical than it creates a story arc: events are tied to the theme but quite generic in flavor. Twilight Struggle has more story. 

This game reminds me the most of Nexus Ops, with its Rebel objectives and the short term effects. 

The rules are quite simple and clear and well laid out. However, there are many of them, and it is a bit hard to set them all in movement, during the first game. Furthermore, a few important details are left to the reference rulebook: the problem is that sometimes we don't know that we should look there. I feel that the game is not too hard to go back to, though, so the situation is not bad. 

The rules make sense thematically, as do the card powers. This is nice. 

Overall  solid game that did not wow me but that I could play again—even if our first game took 5 hours.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Star Wars Rebels n'est pas ce que vous attendez de lui au début. Compte tenu de la taille du plateau et du grand nombre de figurines, on pourrait penser que Star Wars Rebellion est plus un jeu comme Battle of the Five Armies, peut-être même Risk. Cependant, l'accent est beaucoup plus sur les missions de jeu. Vous devez réfléchir aux leaders que vous utilisez et aux leaders que votre adversaire peut utiliser pour contrer la mission. Vous devrez penser tactiquement et l'ordre de vos actions déterminera le résultat de la bataille. Vous ne voulez pas non plus déployer tous vos leaders en mission car vous ne pouvez plus contrecarrer les missions ou déplacer des troupes.
À chaque tour, vous obtenez plus de cartes de mission et plus de leaders avec vous donnant plus de choix et au début cela signifie simplement que vous devez lire beaucoup. Au fur et à mesure que le jeu est joué, vous connaissez mieux les cartes, ce qui rend le jeu un peu plus fluide. Cependant, il reste un jeu de société où vous devez passer les heures nécessaires. Avec un peu de chance, vous trouverez rapidement la base rebelle, mais il est possible que les rebelles puissent ensuite déplacer leur base et ainsi recommencer. Eh bien, pas encore tout à fait, parce que le joueur rebelle choisit 8 cartes du deck droid de la sonde et c'est pourquoi il doit choisir. De ce fait, le pont de la sonde devient naturellement plus petit à mesure que le jeu progresse.
Pour le joueur impérial, il est donc très important qu'il / elle recherche rapidement la base rebelle et que les rebelles veulent saboter et reporter autant que possible. Le jeu vous donne les bonnes cartes et joue aussi très différemment en tant qu'impériaux que lorsque vous jouez avec les rebelles. Ceci est bien sûr bien fait thématiquement. L'impériale est grande et puissante, tandis que les rebelles sont beaucoup moins nombreux et doivent jouer astucieusement!
Les règles ne sont pas difficiles au début, mais là aussi vous devez revenir régulièrement aux règles pour rechercher certains termes, commandes et devis. Graphiquement, tout est beau et bien organisé. Le thème de Star Wars correspond bien, mais quand il a été choisi un thème différent avec, bien sûr, d'autres missions que cela aurait fonctionné en principe.
Alors teamplay. J'ai vraiment aimé jouer en équipe. Vous devez vous consulter et donner à un joueur l'avance sur les généraux (troupes au sol) et l'autre sur les amiraux (vaisseaux spatiaux) avec leurs propres tâches, c'est plus que jouer le même jeu avec plus de joueurs. Ce que nous n'avions pas vu en première instance, c'est que l'ordre est important dans le jeu en équipe. Cela signifie: d'abord les amiraux des deux parties (missions et batailles), puis les généraux. Cela donne au jeu encore plus de tactique et donc il est également nécessaire de consulter. Il est même vrai que je pense que le jeu d'équipe est aussi beau que 1 contre 1, contre mes attentes.
Dans l'ensemble, Star Wars Rebellion est un jeu où vous devez plonger pendant un moment, où vous devez prendre quelques heures et le thème devrait vous plaire. Secrètement, j'espère déjà une expansion avec de nouvelles missions et des personnages d'autres films, mais jusqu'à ce moment-là, je vais encore avoir assez de plaisir avec ce jeu de plateau épique. Est-ce que tout ce qui précède vous ressemble et êtes-vous fan de Star Wars? Ensuite, avec X-Wing, c'est le jeu de plateau ultime pour vous!

RATING: 7
I really like how assymetric the Imperial and Rebel sides are. The Imperial has many more units but needs to find and destroy the Rebel base before time runs out and so need to sweep the galaxy quickly, whereas the Rebels can stall out the game and have more specific tasks via various objectives that can speed up the end of the game. I do wish the game was a little shorter for what it is, but it does give off a feel of a grand epic space hunt. The pseudo-action programming with the leaders is also pretty cool, and you can really counter your opponent's stuff if they don't add extra leaders to bolster. It also adds a layer of strategy via timing your actions so that you have multiple leaders in one location, thus having a higher chance of success. It is kind of annoying at end of game when you have like 8 leaders and need to boost everything to have a chance to do anything, but I like how the game weans you into having more options once you have an idea what you're doing. The actions themselves while having a bunch of repeats also seem to give a good amount of flexibility of how you can play (e.g. I played the Rebels, and I was mostly content to sit back, build up my forces, and snipe opportune objectives, but could have instead played a more risky strategy of trying to end the game quickly via trying to complete them en masse, and fishing for the ones I am close to finishing). My only main negative of this game is the fiddliness of the combat. Between the tactics cards (which are a good idea, but add more overhead), the possible multiple rounds of combat, the two types of damage/health, and ground/air, combat can take quite a while to resolve.

RATING: 9
This game brings the events from a New Hope, Empire Strikes Back, and Return of the Jedi to life.  It can be played 2 or 4 player.  It is really a two player game though.  One player plays the Rebellion and hides the rebel base and wins if the turn count and the mission markers meet on a track.  The empire wins if ground forces are in the Rebel base at the end of the turn.  The Rebels seem to have an advantage for inexperienced players.  

Players either play missions or move troops.  Also, they build new units and gain information about Rebel base locations.  

Many of the events and missions come from the movies.  I really like the game and will play it any chance I get.  It has been called "Star Wars of the Ring".  And I can see the comparison, due to the asymmetry of play, but in general, War of the Ring is a better game. However, this is excellent.

RATING: 3
Wow, I was not expecting to dislike this game so much. I find it very boring and way too long for what it has to offer.

I find the core mechanic of the game not very engaging or interesting. It consists of assigning your leaders/heroes to missions, rolling dice according to your leader's skill level and checking whether you succeed or not. While I am ok with this mechanic in games like Eldrich Horror or Runebound, I very much dislike it here. While this mechanic adds to the feel of adventure and exploration in the former mentioned games, to me it feels misplaced in Star Wars; Rebellion, which at least claims to be a somewhat tactical game. The majority of the game consists of flipping cards and rolling dice. It is not that entertaining and highly random, too. And there are no (or close to no) mechanics that offer you any methods of mitigating that randomness either, like character development/leveling or items or anything of that kind.

The other part of the game looks like a typical area control war game, but it really is not one. You have a bunch of cool looking miniatures, but the game does not play like a miniature war game. The rebel side is hopelessly outnumbered, which makes thematic sense and all, but it feels a little frustrating as the rebel player to be outmatched like this. And on the other side it feels very unsatisfying to fight the rebels as the imperial player, since they are much weaker. On top of it all, the combat system is extremely fiddly. This is especially annoying, considering how little tactical choices you have during combat, if any (and you will hear this complaint even from fans of this game). 

I was surprised that there are no upgrades for your units and that your leaders don't improve in any way (with one exception being Luke who might become a Jedi). In other words, there is no mechanic in this game that allows you to individualize your faction, not even a tiny bit.

I also dislike the fact that you have no choice when to build or what to build. Every two rounds, the building phase triggers and you can only build units, that your loyal or subjugated planets provide. This is one more missed opportunity to individualize your play-style. What if you prefer building more ground units instead of Space units? Well sorry, the game does not allow you to make that decision.

Another point I want to mention is the replayability. After 2 or 3 sessions of this game, you will have seen most or even all of the objective and mission cards. Once you have seen them all, the flavor of the theme gets dull, too. The above mentioned mechanics, boring as they are, will then not even offer any appealing theme or surprises anymore. Also, the board is not randomly set up like in comparable space games, which is another point that lowers the replayability of this game.

Considering how few interesting mechanics this game offers, it plays WAY TOO LONG, too. If it was over after an hour our so, I would be somewhat ok with it (though it would still be a boring game). But flipping cards and rolling dice for 2 to 4 hours is pretty dull and boring.

Bottom line is, for a 3-5 hours game, which kind of wants to be a tactical game, it offers almost no meaningful or interesting decisions or game play options. it is highly restrictive in almost every mechanic. and the only thing it may have going for it is the theme which will be exhausted after 2-3 plays. I mean, how often will it be interesting to capture han solo?

I am puzzled how this game managed to climb up this high in the ratings, but than again it says Star Wars on the box.

RATING: 9

RATING: 9
Ok.  It's another Corey Koniezca game, and to be honest, the mechanics feel a [i]lot[/i] like Runewars in space.  But that is not a bad thing, because Runewars is amazing!  (Original Runewars, not the new Runewars miniatures game.)  There's always a lot going on and you'll never have as many actions as you'd like to take.   Tough decisions every round.   It does deviate from Runewars in that the powers and victory conditions are asymmetrical, and boy, do they perfectly capture the feeling of Star Wars.  This game is So Much Fun you barely notice 3-4 hrs flying by.  

Now, that said, it's not perfect.  It takes a couple reads of the rules, and inevitably some searching online for a FAQ and unclear interactions, to really have a solid grasp of everything.  (Same downside as many FFG games, like Runewars or BSG or AGOT (2d ed) or the GOT card game.)  It's always frustrating to get bogged down in minutiae when you're trying to focus on the overall flow of the game.  The minutiae can be terribly important, so you have to.  Yes, it makes the first couple games tough (so get someone who knows it inside and out to teach you, if possible!).

Overall, I love it.  Have only played 3 games but I'm hoping we'll see much more play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game perfectly captures the feeling of the original Trilogy. It's not an area control game per-say, however gaining an holding territory is needed for goals and advancement. It's more like a PvP hidden movement game, where the Empire attempts to locate and destroy the Rebels (before they can gain to much glory, or run away). 

Gameplay lasts only 7-9 rounds, but playtime is in the 3-4 hours. The central aspect of each round is playing "mission" cards to get better control of systems, learn information, or advance the game clock. Dice are central, but its strongly mitigated by leaders abilities or cleaver misdirection. Besides time, the downside is combat, which is clunky and feels removed from the theme of the game. Combat is fixed with the expansion.    

Purchased: 05/02/16 (Titan)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.7
I really like this game. The only downside for me is the long time it takes to play. The beautiful thing is, that AP is also calculated in the time. Truly a game that fits me (I also really like Star Wars).

I played it with a friend who isn't so much into Star Wars (we didn't even talk about it, we just played the game) and he liked it and wanted to play it at least one time more (he was imperial, I believe he wanted to try the rebels with the next game). So the game is suitable for players who don't like or don't know Star Wars all that well.

The game works perfect online (with help of Vassal en BGG), so you can save and continue the game almost in your own time (and don't need to take the 3-4 hours immediately). I'll wait for my first PBF to end before I comment on the 4-player online... :)

Edit: played a couple of games PBF-style. And 2 of them were 4 player. I love the 3-4 player teamplay of this game. Especially the planning gets another dimension: you can make 2 actions in a row, but you also need to watch what leader goes where, otherwise your plans will fail.

Love the game and upped the rating!

RATING: 8
Successfully evokes the atmosphere of the original Star Wars trilogy. I enjoy the mechanics of using leaders to play missions or move units. (The latter is reminiscent of Twilight Imperium III to me.)

I am not all that convinced that the game is balanced. As the rebel player, one needs to be extremely cautious about not getting leaders captured in the first half because it costs an action per turn and because the follow-up missions for the Imperium are very strong (some more or less force to reveal the location of the basis).

The fighting system is rather boring. Especially the cards are annoying because very often one does not have the required die symbol to use them. Also, there will be few battles that are not predetermined.

RATING: 10
I've heard this game on several occasions be called "Star Wars in a box" and it really is. There are many moments in the game both big and small that feel as though you are playing out your own eerily familiar story that just seems that little bit off.

In my last game Boba Fett and Darth Vader caught Han Solo on Sullust and when Leia came to save him the trap was sprung and she was taken before the Emperor in an attempt to turn her to the Dark Side but she refused to turn and escaped, Little did we know that Luke was headed to Dagobah to complete his training. Shortly after Admiral Ackbar lead an assault on the Death Star as it hung above Malastare with the entire fleet being wiped out expect three small Y-Wings one of which tool that fateful shot to take down the Death Star. The Empire would not give up however and had narrowed down the Rebel Base's location and an evacuation was called, saving their skin in the nick of time.

In terms of the mechanisms they are actually fairly simple but the depth comes in the choices you make, what missions you send your team on, where do you allocate your resources. One hint though. If you are the Empire and want to win "don't get cocky" because you may get all caught up in the fun of your huge fleet and destroying your enemy while they tick down that timer to victory, hidden away.

RATING: 9.9
I knew I was predisposed to like this one with plenty of high quality miniatures (and other superb components, much as you'd expect from any Fantasy Flight Games game these days), asymmetrical conflict, interesting game play and an epic theme.

My first play was not a disappointment. I was the imperials trying to track the rebel (scum) throughout the galaxy and destroy their hidden base. I had an overwhelming superiority in conventional forces but my opponents were wily - hard to find and difficult to engage as they prefer hit-and-run attacks to stand-up slug fests, though occasionally they can be engaged in a conventional manner. As the game progressed, I had narrowed my search to five planets, but the rebel (scum) has managed to quietly achieve a number of their secret objectives cutting down he time I had left. The game climaxed in an epic battle bot on the surface and in the space surrounding the recently-relocated rebel base. My attack was hampered by their commando squads who destroyed our walkers before they could be deployed. This, and some truly lousy work by my stormtroopers, lost us the surface battle even as the sky was alight with burning rebel ships. Jedi Luke Skywalker saw his chance and killed the emperor toppling the Empire and bringing in a new era of peace. Very epic and very true to the ethos of the films.

I really liked the way the game played, plenty of decisions to be made around allocating priorities, assigning leaders and deploying forces. The leader mechanic is particularly entertaining. All of this leads me to conclude there is plenty of replayability in what I am sure will become a classic.

I had very little hesitation in picking this up from a local FOLGS and have every confidence this will get plenty of use for years to come.

Highly recommended.

RATING: 10
Amazing game.  I think the references to Twilight Struggle are appropriate.  This game provides 3 - 4 hours of strategic tension from the get go.  Players have a hand of cards, and each play is a small piece of an unfolding cat-and-mouse on the part of both players.  Just as with Twilight Struggle, hands have to be carefully managed.  Important missions need to be couched in such a way that the opposing player can not appropriately counter them. Like a game of hearts, how a player structures their turn is incredibly important. But regardless of one's best laid plans, the other player will, on occasion, have a play that "wins them" that turn.  A leader is captured and turned to the dark side.  A fighter survives and with a card drop, takes out the Death Star.  With multiple plays, the cards become more familiar, especially those that recur and serve to define the playing style of one side or the other.  But this only deepens the strategic weight - reactions become anticipatory precautions.  Still, given the random draw of cards, sometimes you lose a turn, look at the upcoming turn, and think, "Oh crap, how am I going to get through this one?"  These are experiences very reminiscent of Twilight Struggle.

But the game is not simply Twilight Struggle in space.  It is very much a Star Wars game.  And the reason for this is that the game VERY COOLY focuses on characters.  The most important element of the game -- what players spend most of their time doing -- is assigning characters to missions.  Really, this is just an action selection mechanic, albeit one that is somewhat fluid, but which also wonderfully references the fictional Star Wars universe.  It's not a meeple assigned to "infiltrate" or "sabotage," it is Leah or Chewie.  And further, Leah or Chewie is selected because their abilities make them a slightly better choice for that action than any of the other characters.  So, on any turn each player is assigning a stable of characters to a set of actions that thematically create and reference the StarWars storyline.  Additionally, a few of these characters will become the "stars" of a single game play's unique story.  The reason for this is that in addition to action selection, each player has a few cards that provide a one-off special ability for a character.  There is a modicum of choice about which characters will have this focus, but only just.  So, at a crucial point in the game, it is Wedge who suddenly blows up the Death Star, or Chewie who returns to his home planet to lead an uprising against the Empire garrison.  What I find interesting about this mechanic is that it takes the character-focus of the game, and makes it cinematic.  Players leave the game recalling the memory of how in *that* game, Luke was captured and turned to the dark side.  In *that* game Admiral Ackbar enabled a carnage on both sides of a battle that weakened the Empire just enough to save the Rebel base.

It's for this reason that I also don't mind the combat mechanics.  I've read reviews that assert that the combat mechanics bog down what is an otherwise slick game.  I initially felt that way, too, and it's true, the only weakness of the game for me is the iconography on the dice (it is not intuitive).  True, the combat *does* jerk the rest of the game to a different "place."  Most of the the game consists of "across the universe cat and mouse" with the ominous movement and counter-movement of military forces that gather like storm clouds...and then a battle brings in overly particular elements like dice, choices of ships hit, random card draws, etc.  The thing is, though, I've come to find this to be a very cinematic experience.  It's as if there is a movie that cuts between the goings on on this planet, and the character encounters on *that* planet...but when a big space battle occurs, time contracts to "real time."  There is a bit of tactics, but mostly an actual battle is luck with the strategic deployment being vastly more important.  So, my advice is appreciate the battles as a cinematic moment.  You might get lucky and win, you might get unlucky and lose...but *mostly* whether you win or lose the game is going to come down to strategic selection of actions across multiple turns.

One last comment on the game, I've played other FFG 'IP' games - Battlestar Galactica, War of the Ring, Game of Thrones, etc. As a company, they are pretty good, I think, at deconstructing narratives into games.  That said, many of their other attempts have struck me as fiddly.  The game will contain mechanics that don't flow or are gamist - clunky attempts to reference the features of a story line.  In my opinion Star Wars: Rebellion is the best 'IP' game that FFG has produced.  When it gets down to it, the rules are dirt simple: assign actions (missions), resolve one at a time, refresh.  Any complications are pushed out to a few decks of very clearly worded cards.  There is no need to know the ins and outs of everything on the first play. Just look at your current hand, and wait to learn about additional possibilities when they show up. Also, the board does a great job of providing relevant information (this planet produces x&y which get placed on build queue 2.  Very, very smartly designed system.
  
So the game play is fantastic, and it is a wonderful narrative system.  But what about StarWars?  I'm not a StarWars "fanboy." I don't own the movies; I did not collect the cards (the blue series, orange series, etc. that came in packs of gum); I haven't read a single book or comic; I didn't ever have a Hans figure... but I have friends that did all of this.  And I do love the shared fandom of StarwWars.  I love seeing folks dressed up as Storm Troopers at cons, just like I love that someone took the time to create a single 2-hour movie from the 3 prequels.  I totally get that passionate attachment to a narrative - its possibilities, its familiarity, its sense of participatory, creation.  Like I say, though, StarWars was never quite my thing, even though I will never forget the first time that I saw the original film when it was released back in '77.  And the characters are deeply embedded in the sinews of my cultural body, probably in a way that is similar for Harry Potter to the millennial generation.  So regardless of whether I approach the game as a fan or not, I can't escape the cultural and identity laden vibrations that surround it.  *This* game reignited the feelings of wonder that I experienced when I first saw the original films so many years ago.  It managed to clear out the dreck of branded Happy Meals, branded thermoses, and other cheapening crap.  All in all a fantastic achievement.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Own Rise of the Empire
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
One side is the Galactic Empire, the other side are the Rebels. The Empire has to find the rebel base and occupy it, while the Rebels need to acquire reputation to prevent the Empire from winning. Each side has leaders which allow you to move, attack and undergo missions. 

Combat takes place in space and on the ground. You roll dice to get hits and cards are used to supplement the combat. 

It's a fun, thematic game. There is luck with the dice, and it can be a bit longish. But the tension in having the Empire discover the rebel base, then try to bring their forces to bear is a worthwhile experience. There are a few different things you can try. It will be interesting to see if future games are filled with this tension.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Would always be down for a game! Just be sure to set aside 3-4 hours for a game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
When I heard about Star Wars: Rebellion I thought, 'I've already played that, it was a PC game in the late 90s'. I liked the PC game, in fact I miss playing it, as not even Good Old Games has a fully playable port of the original. I was intrigued, would this board game play like the PC original?

Yes, yes it does. Fantasy Flight didn't create a new board game so much as successfully port a video game to board game format. The basic gameplay is identical. They simplified the units, unit production, space battles, and trimmed down the character and unit variety, but the core game I loved is still there, now in versus mode!.

I predict FFG will release the trimmed Expanded Universe characters and some other ship types in a future expansion, as they're known for that, and for once I don't see it as just a cash grab, the trims were made to simplify play while not removing many elements from the original trilogy that fans would miss.

SW:R is still a long game, epic in scope, on par I'd say with War Of The Ring. The events of the original Star Wars trilogy are able to be recreated to nostalgic effect and fun.

There is a real lack of interesting Rebel missions to attempt, especially when compared with the amount of neat things the Empire player can do.

RATING: 7
I bought this game because of a super sale, not really thinking I'd find anyone to play it with especially my SO. Lo and behold I got him to play and it turned out he loved it! We played 4 games over 2 weeks. Definitely enjoy it, but there are some limitations that keep it from a higher rating from me personally:

1. It can be a bit of a bear to set up. So it's not a game I want to pull out all the time. Typically, a single game can span several after-work evenings, so playing it is really a commitment over several days.

2. For players on the more casual side I think it's really hard for the Imperial player to win. I played rebels pretty poorly in some instances and still managed to win.

3. Some cards, once played are easy for the opponent to avoid in subsequent games, rendering them useless. For example, there is an action card for Obi Wan that if captured I can remove him and gain reputation. My opponent now knows to never capture Obi Wan.

RATING: 10
A fantastic orgy of miniatures, strategy, and space opera drama! There are a plethora of mechanics that intertwine, but players adapt the roles of the sides they choose with Rebels acting like rogues and the Imperial player performing pompous acts with massive displays of force. There is a twitch of delight the first time someone utters the phrase about a certain, "fully armed and operational battle station."

This is a long game with a lot of mechanics. I haven't had a game under 3 hours, yet. Expect to read the rules, then find the official FFG rule clarifications, and then play a few rounds to hone the gameplay. After three or four games, the setup and turn-based action do achieve a certain flow.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A nearly flawless 2-4 player thematic recreation of the original Star Wars trilogy that rests on the shoulders of tightly designed mechanics which reward careful forethought and planning while still allowing enough randomness to make combat and the undertaking of critical missions feel exciting and not scripted.

There is never a boring or dry turn, with every action you take needing to be seriously considered against the myriad (but not overwhelming) number of options available to you every round.

The only minor criticisms I can level against the game are: 1) Large-scale combat tends to drag a bit and be overly fiddly due to the combination of rolling dice and drawing/playing cards. 2) The game is very long, generally clocking in at 5+ hours, despite the box claiming it is a 3-4 hour game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
The ultimate gaming experience for me. Now I can't enjoy any other game as much as before because none of them are closely as good as this one.

Probably wouldn't enjoy it as much if it had a different theme or if I was not a Star Wars fan, but it still is a solid two player game. Can't wait for expansions

Edit:  The main criticism the game gets is its combat system, but it not bad at all. Is good, actually, but as the game is great, maybe "good" doens't feel as good. You can make decisions with the tactic cards that will end up defining lots of things, like, for example, you let a capital ship be destroyed to save some fighters, knowing that you will be able to use those fighters later to destroy the death star that is getting closer and closer, even though in the moment it may seem like a bad idea.

I've played 5 times now, and the replay value is great too. Once you know what kind of cards can appear in the game, you can shape your strategy in ways you couldn't have ever thought before, and your opponent can do things that will have a purpose in the future because he knows that at some point they will. This can make it even more fun than the first couple of times you play it

RATING: 7
規則:
*時間標記放1，榮譽標記放14，目標卡照牌被洗勻疊起數字最小的在最上面，地面跟太空戰術卡分別洗勻，右下方有星號的計畫任務卡洗勻放到圖板對應位置
*每個玩家拿各自陣營配件(黑色帝國，白色反抗)，每個人拿四個右中沒有招募記號的領袖為起始領袖放在玩家圖板的領袖庫，反抗軍玩家抽一張目標卡，所有玩家行動卡洗勻(第一次只使用招募行動卡)放個人圖板右邊，每人拿各自的四張起始任務卡(下方有符號)，所有剩下任務卡雙方各自洗勻放個人圖板左邊，放起始單位跟榮譽標記，反抗軍從每有帝國單位的星球卡選一張當基地差到主圖板對應區，其他洗勻放置對應位置(第一場建議選不要相鄰帝國軍的)，每人在各自抽兩張任務卡
*遊戲進行數輪，每輪有三個階段
1.分配任務階段 反抗軍先開始，蓋著放任意張任務卡，每張上面放一或兩個領袖，然後換帝國軍
2.命令階段 反抗軍開始，輪流行動二選一直到都跳過，選擇跳過就不再行動
>啟動一個星系 放一個領袖到你要啟動的星系格，此時可以移動相鄰星系(沒有你的領袖的)的太空船到該星系，每個太空船可帶其容量的地面單位，如果該星系有敵方單位觸發戰鬥，如果領袖左下跟右下沒有數字不能做此行動
*圖板總共有32個星系，每個星系周圍有黑色的太空區放太空船，下方有藍色資源跟六腳格會資源星系，否則為遙遠星系，紅色區域不能通過，橘色是邊界，橘色邊界把圖板分成八個區域
*當帝國軍放下地面單位到星系時，如果是反抗軍隱藏基地
>揭開任務卡  選擇打開一張任務卡並選擇要結算的星系放置(如果再隱藏基地則直接放到圖板基地處)，如果有attemp字樣，對方可放1領袖在該星系上(沒放就直接成功)，然後彼此都擲骰，每個領袖能力有對應該任務卡的可骰一顆，骰出的結果要大於對方才成功，起始任務使用後會回手，其他的棄掉
3.重整階段  所有領袖回領袖庫，沒使用的任務回手，每人抽兩張任務卡(超過10張要棄)，帝國玩家抽兩張星系卡，反抗軍玩家抽一張任務卡，時間軌前進一格，根據該格可招募或建造，然後所有建造列的單位向下移動1格，1的可直接放在有你榮譽標記的星系，每個星系最多兩個，有敵軍的星系不能建造或放單位
>招募  抽兩張行動卡，選一張拿該領袖，卡片移除
>建造 每個有榮譽標記星系造一個單位，要符合該星系資源標記(帝國軍反面壓迫標記則只能使用最左邊資源符號)，建造的單位放到對應資源欄數字的生產列上
**帝國玩家找到隱藏基地且消滅所有單位後上面有自己單位獲勝，反抗軍在時間跟名譽軌重疊時獲勝，任務卡左上數字在完成時可降低名譽軌(每次戰鬥跟重整階段只能出一張)
*當隱藏基地被放帝國榮耀標記或地面單位時就被發現，所有反抗軍單位移動到對應星系上，之後不再使用隱藏基地，建新基地任務時抽四張星球卡選一張新的當隱藏基地，舊的要打開給帝國玩家，且單位移動到該星系上，被放置破壞標記的資源都不能使用
*當玩家在星系獲得榮譽時就放一個榮譽標記，如果本來是別人的則移除，如果有星系上面有帝國玩家的地面單位可放榮譽標記背面的壓迫標記(可放到反抗軍榮譽標記上)
*領袖靈氣最多只能有一個，被帝國捕抓的領袖變成帝國地面單位，但最多只能抓一個，抓第二個第一個就釋放，當被捕抓的領袖周圍沒有帝國軍就被釋放
**戰鬥**
>沒有戰術值的領袖在該星系時可以增加一個
>每個玩家根據領袖的戰術值，抽對應的卡牌張數(多的只用數字高的那個)
>戰鬥階段 雙方都有船時，發動玩家全部船攻擊一次在換對手攻擊一次，然後換結算地面單位各攻擊一次，然後雙方可選擇撤退，否則重複空戰跟陸戰
*戰鬥時加總單位的黑紅數值拿對應骰數(上限各5)，擲完骰後可先使用戰術卡(可能要支付骰)或棄對應骰面抽戰術卡，然後分配骰點傷害給對方，只能分配對應血量顏色的骰子(有個骰面可不管顏色)，防守方可出戰術卡檔傷害，掛點的單位依然可以在該輪攻擊沒掛的放傷害標記在模型下方，戰鬥結束後全部移除
*撤退時遵守移動規則，沒有領袖不能撤退，帝國軍在死星不能撤退，要優先撤退到有你榮譽標記或單位的相鄰星系，不能撤到有敵方單位或是敵方進攻來的星系
**進階規則**
非招募行動卡一開始隨機抽兩張，遊戲中可使用一次
可使用抽牌規則放置起始星系跟單位

RATING: 8
Asymmetry is always valued in a balanced game. Can't speak to the overall balance, but can speak to the really nice decision matrix the game provides. It has an eerie sense of LotR LCG. There, leaders choose to quest, defend, or attack. Here your leaders quest (do a mission), trigger a move/attack, or hang back to defend. This similarity is a good thing - it's driven 500+ games of the LCG. It makes for continual hard and interesting decisions. These are influenced by how much energy you're putting into your strategic vs tactical imperatives, and there are different strategies to employ which will certainly engender replay. I also like how the space/ground theatres in combat drives what systems you want to "colonise" so as to build the units you want and when you want them. And the components are top class, as you'd expect from FFG. All good stuff, and looking forward to more play.

RATING: N/A
Impressive looking and exciting asymmetric game. Tho' it has the semblance of a war game, it is essentially a worker placement game: the 'generals' are assigned for the actions that take or enable. In this game, the Rebels are completely outgunned and cannot hope to defeat the Empire militarily; what they have to do is survive to the end of the game (which they can try to hasten), while the Empire needs to find and take control of the Rebels' hidden base before they run out of time.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
(5+ plays)  Once you get into the Star Wars mindset, and pay attention to your characters, and imagine the story each character is playing out each mission - this starts to feel like the best questing game around.  Unlike countless hero questing wargame hybrids before it, every mission MATTERS, both on the battlefield, AND for the individual plot developments on which the hero character missions hang.  They've nailed this, and it's only a matter of time before some decent fantasy games finally achieve what this game has.  

The epic strategy and leader decision trade-offs make the core of the game fun and set up some dramatic events.  I think it was more fun to play the rebels.  My Imperial opponent commented that the strategy for him was pretty straight-forward, and he was just waiting for me to annoy with cards to frustrate his plans.  In some ways it did feel like that, where I was saving cards and planning out moves to destroy the Death Star and push forces back just as they were approaching the rebel base.  Is the inevitability of the Imperial conquest just as fun as the Rebel spoilers?  I'm not sure yet.  My first game was the dark side, and I've played 4 of 5 games as the Rebels.

I have mixed feelings about the combat system.  On the one hand, I've decided I really like the balance and results.  If you go into a battle well-prepared with a good leader, things are very likely to go well.  When you are fighting an important battle on which a mission or objective is tied, the combat is fun and dramatic.  The dice rolls and card play make sense, and concentrating fire (or not) seems a tactical battle decision that is thematic and works well.

However, it's particularly frustrating when you attack a location with an overwhelming force, and it takes three rounds of combat to destroy one X-wing.  There is a lot of bluff and double bluff going on in the game.  That one X-wing might take out a tie fighter or two or three.  And in certain systems, with certain conditions, that could make all the difference now or next turn.  More often, there are other systems where it doesn't matter at all.  BUT if I make that clear, and shorten the combat - I'm giving away some information.  Sooooo, even for the entirely meaningless battles, I play out the boring 5 minutes, because I am giving away information if I don't.

Overall, this is a personal favorite that I wish I could play over and over again.  Right now, it's not a 10 because I think an expansion or a second edition could improve a few things slightly (and that probably will happen).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Best long two player game I  have played. Intense right until the end.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The big box game many Star Wars fans have been waiting for. A truly epic game with phenomenal production value that you will be thinking about days after playing. Rebellion is more tactical than strategic and you have to be able to adapt. This is not a risk like game since the Rebellion military forces are primarily used to delay, feint and surgically strike not overwhelm. If you expect otherwise you will likely be disappointed. Don't waste your time with the intro game and jump into the advanced setup, you will not be disappointed.

Pros:
* I cannot say enough about the component quality.
* Destroying planets with the Death Star never gets old.
* Huge game board with a clean layout.
* Tons of miniatures.
* 4 players worked flawlessly.

Cons:
* Games can run long.
* Setup can take some time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Excellent epic two player strategy game. Certainly on one level with War of the Ring, for me actually a bit above.

Many say this, but it is true: SW Rebellion is Star Wars in a box. The theme is just excellently captured in this game. The card driven actions are very enjoyable and yield  a good combination of strategy and tactics. The asymmetry between Empire and Rebels is huge, but still it seems balanced to me. Combat rules are simple, which fits perfect for a game of such a greats scope. Components are very good (even though too much air in the box for my taste). 

I am of the rare breed that actually enjoy the combat. There is quite a bit of randomness with rolling dice and  drawing cards that may work  perfect or are currently useless. But for longer fights there is enough randomness to even out to some degree, but still has the chance to generate some drama. The card can be quite relevant and hence a leader that gives you two or three cards (while you opponent chooses not to send a leader) can have a significant effect. However, I am not into wargames and  may be not aware of battle systems that are much more engaging.

My biggest complaint is the box which could really be a bit flatter to require less shelf space.

RATING: 8
This is an overall excellent asymmetric head to head strategy game. It takes quite a while to set up and tear down, with also a very long play time. Almost every game I've played has come down to one or two moves that were easily identifiable as game deciding when examined in hind sight; to me this is a great sign that choices matter.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Impressive integration of Star Wars theme with engaging mechanics. Secret objectives, desperate missions, terror in the galaxy, heroic last stands,  all driven by characters from the movies. And it all hangs together in FFGs overwrought, shambolic manner. Of course there are eight decks of cards - I honestly believe FFG sends any designer of a big box game back to the drawing board if it doesn't feature at least eight decks of cards and 10 different kinds of tokens. 

But you knew that already. This is a game of card draws, dice pools, and hundreds of bits, calling to mind War of the Ring. However the scope of strategy isn't as narrow as that game. There's more going on across a more widely dispersed arena. 

Still, this isn't a game where you go back and think about how you would approach a problem differently next time, or employ a dramatically different strategy. The game, especially for the Rebellion, is going to be driven by your objectives, and often your course of action will be obvious. And if you don't draw the right missions or objectives... well, you just hang on desperately hoping that the card draw swing back in your favour. 

It's fun enough if played for the narrative experience generated - Leia sneaks into the Death Star to rescue Chewbacca! But I don't know that there's enough genuine game heft to warrant 3-4 hours, especially if the luck of the draw starves you of genuine options.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
So it got here.  And I've played three games with my family.

I love it.

I haven't rated it a 10 yet, because I need more plays to figure out if it's a ten.  It needs time for me to see if there are multiple layers of strategies and interesting interactions.  I think they're there, but I'm not 100% sure yet.  If it holds up to the test of time it's a 10 for sure.

But boy, it punches every one of my original trilogy buttons.  It's got epic battles.  It's got characters pulling underhanded stuff.  It's got Death Stars, and Death Star trench runs.  It's got that cat-and-mouse feel between the Empire and the Rebellion.

It's everything I could ever want from a Star Wars grand strategy game, in a terrific, beautiful package.  And there's all kinds of tension in the decision-making in the game system.

I'm looking for players for this one, and I'll play it anytime someone wants to come over and have fun with it.

Update, 1/3/17: Yep, it's a 10.  It's got replayability, too.  Everything about this one is so very well designed, and I don't feel like it lacks for anything.  It's tight, and there are strategies and counter-strategies.

And it's got a strong play-by-forum community here on the 'Geek, which is wonderful.  And it plays well in that format!
